See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § modified frog kick" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#modified_frog_kick" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">modified frog kick</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="frogman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">frogman</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Frogman" title="Frogman">Frogman</a></span></p>
A scuba diver, particularly a military diver on an undercover mission.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fsw" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fsw</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#feet_sea_water"><span title="See entry on this page at § feet sea water" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">feet sea water</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="full_duplex" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">full duplex</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Duplex_(telecommunications)#Full_duplex" title="Duplex (telecommunications)">Duplex (telecommunications)#Full duplex</a></span></p>
Voice communication system where both users can transmit and receive at the same time. Compare with <a href="#full_duplex">half duplex</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="full-face_mask" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">full-face mask</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Full-face_diving_mask" title="Full-face diving mask">Full-face diving mask</a></span></p>
Diving mask covering the eyes, nose and mouth, and which provides the diver with breathing gas</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="G">G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ga">Ga</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="gap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § jump" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#jump" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">jump</a></span></span></p> 
The space between two cave guidelines. Usually between a main guideline and the start tie-off of a branch line.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gap_spool" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gap spool</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Distance_line#Spools" title="Distance line">Distance line#Spools</a></span></p>
A relatively short length of cave line on a spool used to bridge a gap between lines when making an excursion from the main guideline to a branch guideline. The line is left in place during the excursion, and usually retrieved on the way out</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gaiter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gaiter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "gator" (US)</span></p> Textile legging wrapped around the calf and ankle area over a dry suit to restrict the amount of air that can get into the lower leg area. Also can reduce drag of the suit in this area by smoothing over creases and folds.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="gas_blender" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas blender</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Person who mixes breathing gases for diving, filling <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder" title="Diving cylinder">diving cylinders</a> with gas mixes such as <a href="/wiki/Nitrox" title="Nitrox">nitrox</a> or <a href="/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)" title="Trimix (breathing gas)">trimix</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Certification of competence to mix breathing gases for diving.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_blending" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas blending</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving" title="Gas blending for scuba diving">Gas blending for scuba diving</a></span></p>
Mixing breathing gases for diving, filling <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder" title="Diving cylinder">diving cylinders</a> with gas mixes such as <a href="/wiki/Nitrox" title="Nitrox">nitrox</a> or <a href="/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)" title="Trimix (breathing gas)">trimix</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_block" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas block</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#gas_switching_block"><span title="See entry on this page at § gas switching block" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gas switching block</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="gas_embolism" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas embolism</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gas_embolism" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas embolism">Gas embolism</a></span></p>
Blockage of a blood vessel by a bubble of gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_extender" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas extender</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Carbon dioxide scrubber used to allow partial recirculation of surface-supplied or scuba breathing gas to reduce waste. A form of <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Semi-closed_circuit_rebreathers" title="Rebreather">semi-closed circuit rebreather</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gaseous_impurities" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gaseous impurities</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Contaminants in the compressed breathing air or gas mixture which are in gaseous form. Compare with particulate and condensate impurities.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_integration" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas integration</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="gas-integrated_dive_computer" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas-integrated dive computer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Gas-integrated_dive_computer" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas-integrated dive computer">Gas-integrated dive computer</a></span></p>
Technology to display gas pressure in a scuba cylinder on a dive computer, and in some cases make further use of the information for gas management.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_fraction" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas fraction</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gas_composition" title="Gas composition">Gas composition</a></span></p>
The fraction by molecular count, volume or pressure (they all come to the same thing) of a specific gas in a mixture of gases.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_matching" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas matching</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Gas_matching" title="Scuba gas planning">Scuba gas planning#Gas matching</a></span></p>
The calculation of reserve and turn pressures for divers using different cylinder volumes on the same dive, allowing each diver to ensure that sufficient gas is retained at all times to allow for foreseeable contingencies based on each diver's cylinder volumes, and both divers' individual gas consumption rates.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_narcosis" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas narcosis</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § inert gas narcosis" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#inert_gas_narcosis" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">inert gas narcosis</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="gas_panel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas panel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Gas_panel" title="Surface-supplied diving">Surface-supplied diving#Gas panel</a></span></p>
The control equipment for providing breathing gas to surface supplied divers via umbilicals. Primary and reserve gas is supplied to the panel through shutoff valves from low pressure compressors or high pressure storage cylinders.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_reversal_point" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas reversal point</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The depth during an ascent or decompression when the intake of dissolved gas is exceeded by outgassing.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_sensor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas sensor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A component that produces a signal in the presence of a specific gas, often in proportion to the concentration of the gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_switching" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas switching</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Gas_switching" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas switching">Gas switching</a></span></p>
The procedure of changing from one breathing gas mixture to another during a dive. This may be done to avoid oxygen toxicity, hypoxia, or nitrogen narcosis, to accelerate decompression, or to avoid running out of breathing gas. Generally applied to open circuit breathing equipment, where a physical change-over of gas source is made. In closed circuit systems the gas composition is continuously controlled to follow the chosen <span title="See entry on this page at § set-point" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#set-point" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">set-point</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_switching_block" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas switching block</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A valve set used for switching from one breathing gas to another during a dive. The most common application is a <span title="See entry on this page at § bailout block" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bailout_block" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bailout block</a></span>, but also used to switch gases for decompression on a full face mask, and to switch between deep and shallow gases on a semi-closed rebreather.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gauge_mode" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gauge mode</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dive_computer#Additional_functionality_and_features" title="Dive computer">Dive computer#Additional functionality and features</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dive_computer#Management_of_violations" title="Dive computer">Dive computer#Management of violations</a></span></p>
Operating mode for a personal dive computer where the decompression calculation is disabled, and the unit operated only as a timer and depth gauge. Typically used when diving with gas mixtures not supported by the algorithm, in which case decompression tables are used to monitor and control the decompression schedule. Some dive computers will automatically switch to gauge mode if the diver violates a depth limit, leaving the diver without decompression information.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gauge_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gauge pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pressure_measurement#Absolute,_gauge_and_differential_pressures_-_zero_reference" title="Pressure measurement">Pressure measurement#Absolute, gauge and differential pressures - zero reference</a></span></p>
Gauge pressure is zero-referenced against ambient air pressure, so it is equal to absolute pressure minus atmospheric pressure</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gauge_snubber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gauge snubber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Needle_valve" title="Needle valve">needle valve</a> or small bore orifice between the pressure supply and the gauge which damps pressure fluctuations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gay-lussac&#39;s_law" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Gay-Lussac's law</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gay-Lussac%27s_law" title="Gay-Lussac&#39;s law">Gay-Lussac's law</a></span></p>
Relation between temperature and pressure in an ideal gas for a constant volume.</dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ge">Ge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dt class="glossary" id="general_gas_equation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">general gas equation</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="general_gas_law" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">general gas law</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Relation between the variables pressure, volume and temperature for a given mass of a given mixture of an ideal gas.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Thermodynamic equation of state for gases for the variables volume, pressure, temperature and number and atomic weight of molecules.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="giant_stride_entry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">giant stride entry</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § stride entry" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#stride_entry" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">stride entry</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="glossopharangeal_insufflation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">glossopharangeal insufflation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "buccal pumping", "lung packing"</span></p>
A method used by <a href="/wiki/Freediving" title="Freediving">freedivers</a> for filling the lungs with more air than maximal inspiration to normal total lung capacity (TLC). After a full inhalation, the diver fills the mouth with air, while the glottis remains closed, then opens the glottis and forces this air into the lung using the cheeks and tongue to reduce the mouth volume. This may be repeated several times.<sup id="cite_ref-Potkin_et_al_2007_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Potkin_et_al_2007-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="glowstick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">glowstick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A single-use, translucent plastic tube containing isolated substances that, when combined, make light through chemiluminescence</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gnarly" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gnarly</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A general purpose adjective to denote a particularly difficult section of a cave, which may be low, tight, silty, etc. or a combination.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Go">Go</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Go">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dt class="glossary" id="go_into_decompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">go into decompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Incur a decompression obligation. Generally refers to having a theoretical tissue inert gas concentration that requires the diver to make staged decompression stops during ascent to avoid an unacceptable risk of symptomatic decompression sickness according to the decompression model, algorithm, tables or dive computer in use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="golden_rule" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">golden rule</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The convention in cave diving that anyone can turn the dive at any time for any reason.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gold_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gold line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The permanent main guideline in a cave system, that usually starts well inside the cave. Often yellow or gold in colour.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="goodman_handle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Goodman handle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A handle used to carry the primary dive light head comprising a rigid slot through which the fingers and palm of the hand are extended, so that the light rests on the back of the hand, facing the direction of the extended fingers.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gps" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">GPS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">Global Positioning System</a></span></p>
A satellite navigation system that provides location and time information in all weather, anywhere on or near the Earth, where there is an unobstructed line of sight to four or more GPS satellites</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gradient_factor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gradient factor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Gradient_factors" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Gradient factors</a></span></p>
A way of modifying the <span title="See entry on this page at § M-value" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#M-value" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">M-values</a></span> of a decompression algorithm to more conservative values in proportion to depth. Often used to bias the algorithm towards deeper stops by using a smaller value for the deeper value.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="guide_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">guide line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#distance_line"><span title="See entry on this page at § distance line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">distance line</span></a></span></p></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="habitat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">habitat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Underwater_habitat" title="Underwater habitat">Underwater habitat</a></span></p> 
An underwater structure inside which divers can carry out dry welding or which is fitted out with life support facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="haldanean" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Haldanean</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="haldanian" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">Haldanian</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Critical_ratio_hypothesis" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Critical ratio hypothesis</a></span></p>
Decompression models based on the principles described by <a href="/wiki/John_Scott_Haldane" title="John Scott Haldane">John Scott Haldane</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="half+200" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">half+200</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="half+15" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">half+15</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_gas_management#Rule_of_thumb_gas_planning" title="Scuba gas management">Scuba gas management#Rule of thumb gas planning</a></span></p>
An alternative reserve calculation strategy to the <span title="See entry on this page at § rule of thirds" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#rule_of_thirds" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">rule of thirds</a></span> for breathing stage cylinders. The cylinder is breathed down to half of its starting pressure plus 200&#160;psi (or 15 bar), so that a stage cylinder filled to 3000&#160;psi would be breathed down to 1700 psi before being dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> This is a less conservative strategy for pressures greater than 1200&#160;psi.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="half_duplex" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">half duplex</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Duplex_(telecommunications)#Half_duplex" title="Duplex (telecommunications)">Duplex (telecommunications)#Half duplex</a></span></p>
Voice communications system where users take turns to send and receive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="half_mask" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">half mask</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_mask" title="Diving mask">Diving mask</a></span></p> 
Diver's mask which covers the eyes and nose but not the mouth.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="half_times" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">half times</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § tissue half times" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#tissue_half_times" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">tissue half times</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="halocline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">halocline</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Halocline" title="Halocline">Halocline</a></span></p>
A strong variation in salinity over a small depth range within a body of water. Often visible as a blurred or shimmering region due to uneven refractive index.<sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hand-off_cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hand-off cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A diving cylinder, complete with regulator, which can be handed off (manually transferred) to another diver in an emergency, so that the two divers are not obliged to remain in close proximity during the exit and ascent. Transfer of a hand-off cylinder should not compromise either diver's buoyancy to the extent that they cannot make a normal, controlled ascent at neutral buoyancy.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hang" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hang</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To remain stationary at a specific depth and location, particularly when decompressing.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hang-off" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hang-off</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="hang_off" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">hang off</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dive_profile#Hang-off_profile" title="Dive profile">Dive profile#Hang-off profile</a></span></p>
Commercial diving procedure where the diver ascends to a shallower depth to minimise in-gassing during periods of waiting for surface support. The diver generally ascends to 30 ft waiting depth, and bottom time at that depth is not counted towards decompression obligation. When the support is ready, the diver returns to working depth and time elapsed from leaving hang-off depth accumulates towards decompression obligation. The profile appearance approximates a square wave form, or yo-yo profile.<sup id="cite_ref-Overland_1999_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overland_1999-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hard_hat_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hard hat diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Surface_supplied_diving" class="mw-redirect" title="Surface supplied diving">Surface supplied diving</a>, generally in <a href="/wiki/Professional_diving" title="Professional diving">professional diving</a>, either wearing a modern <a href="/wiki/Diving_helmet" title="Diving helmet">diving helmet</a> or the old-style <a href="/wiki/Standard_diving_dress" title="Standard diving dress">standard diving dress</a> with copper helmet.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hardwire_communications" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hardwire communications</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Voice communications using a cable for transmission.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="harness" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">harness</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Straps and webbing with associated buckles, D-rings and other accessories used to support the breathing apparatus and secure it to the diver. The harness often has other functions such as supporting weighting and buoyancy control systems and for recovery of the diver from the water. In professional diving the harness is used as a strong point to attach the lifeline or umbilical to the diver.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Commercial diver term for <a href="/wiki/Diving_helmet" title="Diving helmet">diving helmet</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hazid" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HAZID</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hazard_identification" class="mw-redirect" title="Hazard identification">Hazard identification</a> study: A systematic qualitative assessment of potential hazards and threats to health, safety, equipment, property, environment, production, or reputation. May be followed by a <a href="/wiki/Risk_assessment" title="Risk assessment">risk assessment</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hazmat_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hazmat diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hazmat_diving" title="Hazmat diving">Hazmat diving</a></span></p>
Diving in a known hazardous materials environment. The environment may be contaminated by hazardous materials, the diving medium may be inherently a hazardous material, or the environment in which the diving medium is situated may include hazardous materials with a significant risk of exposure to these materials to members of the diving team. Special precautions, equipment and procedures are associated with hazmat diving.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="He">He</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: He">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="head-up_display" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">head-up display</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "HUD"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Head-up_display" title="Head-up display">Head-up display</a></span></p>
A visual display mounted where it is normally in the diver's field of vision.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="health_and_safety_executive" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Health and Safety Executive</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "HSE"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_and_Safety_Executive" title="Health and Safety Executive">Health and Safety Executive</a></span></p> 
UK government department responsible for occupational diver safety in UK.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heavy_gear" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">heavy gear</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § standard diving dress" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#standard_diving_dress" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">standard diving dress</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="heliair" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">heliair</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)" title="Trimix (breathing gas)">Trimix (breathing gas)</a></span></p>
Trimix blends made by topping up helium with air.<sup id="cite_ref-Scuba_engineer_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scuba_engineer-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="helicopter_turn" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">helicopter turn</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Manoeuver in which a horizontally trimmed diver uses small fin movements to rotate on the spot on a vertical axis.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heliox" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">heliox</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Heliox" title="Heliox">Heliox</a></span></p>
Mixtures of helium and oxygen for use as a breathing gas.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Scuba_engineer_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scuba_engineer-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="helium" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">helium</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Helium" title="Helium">Helium</a></span></p>
An <a href="/wiki/Inert_gas" title="Inert gas">inert gas</a> which is used as a component of <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">breathing gas</a> mixtures for <a href="/wiki/Deep_diving" title="Deep diving">deep diving</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="helium_analyzer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">helium analyzer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Helium_analyzer" title="Helium analyzer">Helium analyzer</a></span></p>
An instrument used to identify the presence and concentration of helium in a mixture of gases</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="helium_unscrambler" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">helium unscrambler</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="helium_speech_unscrambler" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">helium speech unscrambler</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § speech unscrambler" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#speech_unscrambler" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">speech unscrambler</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="helmet_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">helmet diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#hard_hat_diving"><span title="See entry on this page at § hard hat diving" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hard hat diving</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="henry&#39;s_law" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Henry's law</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Description of the changes in solubility of a given gas in a given liquid as pressure varies.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hi">Hi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="hid_light" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HID light</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/High_intensity_discharge" class="mw-redirect" title="High intensity discharge">High intensity discharge</a> light: Used in cave diving <a href="#light_head"><span title="See entry on this page at § light head" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">light heads</span></a> (q.v.).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hira" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HIRA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Hazard Identification and Risk Analysis: A <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">risk management</a> procedure for identifying hazards and assessing the risk associated with them and ways to reduce the risk to an acceptable level.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ho">Ho</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ho">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="hogarthian_configuration" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Hogarthian configuration</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A scuba combination of backplate, wing, one-piece harness with crotch-strap, regulator arrangement including long-hose primary with a necklaced secondary demand valve, and, if used with twin cylinders, an isolation manifold. Named after <a href="/wiki/William_Hogarth_Main" title="William Hogarth Main">William Hogarth Main</a>, a developer and proponent of the system.<sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hog_looped" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Hog looped</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A scuba configuration where the primary demand valve has a <a href="#long_hose"><span title="See entry on this page at § long hose" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">long hose</span></a> which is routed under the right arm, usually tucked under a light battery canister on the waist belt of the harness, and around behind the neck to reach the mouth from the right hand side. Part of the <a href="#hogarthian_configuration"><span title="See entry on this page at § Hogarthian configuration" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Hogarthian configuration</span></a> (q.v.).<sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hold-back_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hold-back line</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="hold-back_rigging" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">hold-back rigging</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Rigging provided to restrain excessive buoyancy of a <a href="/wiki/Lifting_bag" title="Lifting bag">lifting bag</a> when it is attached to the load and inflated.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="homebrew" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">homebrew</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Amateur blended <a href="#mixed_gas"><span title="See entry on this page at § mixed gas" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">mixed gas</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hood" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hood</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Close-fitting thermal head protection, usually neoprene foam, but also latex on some dry suits.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hook_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hook breathing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § recovery breathing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#recovery_breathing" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">recovery breathing</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="hooka" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hooka</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="hookah" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hookah</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § airline diving" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#airline_diving" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">airline diving</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="hopcalite" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hopcalite</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hopcalite" title="Hopcalite">Hopcalite</a></span></p>
Catalyst sometimes used in breathing air compressor filters to oxidise carbon monoxide to carbon dioxide. Hopcalite is a mixture of manganese oxide, copper oxide and a small amount of silver oxide.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="horse_collar" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">horse collar</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § adjustable buoyancy life jacket" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#adjustable_buoyancy_life_jacket" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">adjustable buoyancy life jacket</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="hose_dash_size" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hose dash size</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Number indicating the bore of a hose in multiples of 1/16" preceded by a dash. for example a –04 hose, typically used for a pneumofathometer hose would have a nominal bore of <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1020198016">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">4</span></span> inch (6.4&#160;mm).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hose_organiser" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hose organiser</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: hose tidy</span></p>
Equipment to position and stabilise a hose, particularly in the context of sidemount or sling mounted scuba cylinders, where the regulator air hoses are stored against the cylinder when not in use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hot_mix" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hot mix</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A breathing gas mixture with a high percentage of oxygen for the depth at which it is used. Using a gas mixture with a high partial pressure of oxygen.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hot_water_suit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hot water suit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_suit#Hot_water_suits" title="Diving suit">Diving suit#Hot water suits</a></span></p>
A loose fitting wetsuit supplied with heated water through a hose in the <a href="/wiki/Diver%27s_umbilical" class="mw-redirect" title="Diver&#39;s umbilical">diver's umbilical</a>, which links the diver to the surface support. The diver controls the flow rate of the water, allowing them to vary the warmth of the suit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hp" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">High pressure, generally gas pressures in excess of 30&#160;bar. In most of the world a high pressure diving cylinder is a 300&#160;bar cylinder, but in the US it may refer to anything over 3000&#160;psi working pressure. In a diving context gas working pressures do not frequently exceed 300&#160;bar, but pressures in hydraulic systems and high pressure water jetting equipment may be considerably higher.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hpns" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HPNS</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="high-pressure_nervous_syndrome" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">high-pressure nervous syndrome</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/High-pressure_nervous_syndrome" title="High-pressure nervous syndrome">High-pressure nervous syndrome</a></span></p>
A neurological and physiological diving disorder that occurs when a diver descends below about 500 feet (150&#160;m) while breathing a helium–oxygen mixture.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hrc" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HRC</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="#hyperbaric_rescue_capsule"><span title="See entry on this page at § hyperbaric rescue capsule" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hyperbaric rescue capsule</span></a></dd> 
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="#hyperbaric_rescue_chamber"><span title="See entry on this page at § hyperbaric rescue chamber" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hyperbaric rescue chamber</span></a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hru" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HRU</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#hyperbaric_rescue_unit"><span title="See entry on this page at § hyperbaric rescue unit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hyperbaric rescue unit</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="hse" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HSE</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#health_and_Safety_Executive"><span title="See entry on this page at § Health and Safety Executive" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Health and Safety Executive</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hu">Hu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="hud" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">HUD</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#head-up_display"><span title="See entry on this page at § Head-up display" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Head-up display</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="h-valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">H-valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Dual_outlet_valves" title="Scuba cylinder valve">Scuba cylinder valve#Dual outlet valves</a></span></p>
Cylinder valve body with two outlets and two valve mechanisms which can be independently controlled so that two regulator first stages can be fitted. Similar to Y-valve but in configuration where the second valve is parallel to the primary, though the secondary valve can sometimes be swivelled.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hydro" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hydro</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Slang/abbreviation for <a href="#hydrostatic_test"><span title="See entry on this page at § hydrostatic test" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hydrostatic test</span></a> (q.v.)<sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hydrophobic_membrane" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hydrophobic membrane</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A membrane that is freely permeable to gas but does not allow the passage of water at low pressure differentials.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hydrostatic_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hydrostatic pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hydrostatic_pressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrostatic pressure">Hydrostatic pressure</a></span></p>
Pressure due to the weight of the water column above a point at depth.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hydrostatic_test" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hydrostatic test</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hydrostatic_test" title="Hydrostatic test">Hydrostatic test</a></span></p>
Non-destructive test to revalidate pressure vessels which uses water as a test medium. The vessel is pressurised to the <span title="See entry on this page at § test pressure" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#test_pressure" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">test pressure</a></span> (q.v.) and measured for permanent set.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hydreliox" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hydreliox</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Hydreliox" title="Hydreliox">Hydreliox</a></span></p>
Deep diving <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">breathing gas</a> mixture of hydrogen, helium and oxygen.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hydrox" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hydrox</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hydrox_(breathing_gas)" title="Hydrox (breathing gas)">Hydrox (breathing gas)</a></span></p>
Deep diving <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">breathing gas</a> mixture of hydrogen and oxygen.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperbaric_evacuation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperbaric evacuation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Evacuation of divers under pressure from a saturation chamber to a hyperbaric rescue craft via a pressurised transfer system.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperbaric_evacuation_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperbaric evacuation system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">System for evacuating divers under pressure from a saturation system in an emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The whole system set up to provide hyperbaric evacuation, including planning, procedures, equipment used for evacuation, reception facility, contingency plans, possible safe havens and anything else requited for a successful hyperbaric evacuation.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperbaric_lifeboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperbaric lifeboat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A lifeboat with a hyperbaric chamber and life support system built into it for evacuating saturation divers in an emergency.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperbaric_rescue_capsule" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperbaric rescue capsule</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A self contained buoyant hyperbaric chamber intended for emergency evacuation of saturation divers under pressure from a platform which has become so dangerous that it is considered safer to put the divers into the sea in the HRC to be picked up by a rescue vessel for transfer to another hyperbaric system for decompression.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperbaric_rescue_chamber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperbaric rescue chamber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Normally a pressure vessel adapted to function as a means of hyperbaric evacuation with buoyancy chambers and lifting points, but not fitted in a lifeboat hull.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperbaric_evacuation_unit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperbaric evacuation unit</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="hyperbaric_rescue_unit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperbaric rescue unit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "HEU", "HRU"</span></p>
Generic term for the unit provided to evacuate divers from a saturation system. It may be an <a href="#hRC"><span title="See entry on this page at § HRC" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">HRC</span></a> or a <span title="See entry on this page at § SPHL" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#SPHL" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">SPHL</a></span> or some other suitable pressure vessel.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hypercapnia" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hypercapnia</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hypercapnia" title="Hypercapnia">Hypercapnia</a></span></p>
Excessive level of carbon dioxide in the body.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperfilter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperfilter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving" title="Gas blending for scuba diving">Gas blending for scuba diving#</a></span></p>
Additional filter to produce air of oxygen compatible quality, usually for partial pressure gas blending. This may be built into the filling system or temporarily connected when required.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperoxic_linearity" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperoxic linearity</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Property of an oxygen sensor to produce linear output at partial pressures above the highest calibration point.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperventilation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperventilation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A deliberate <a href="/wiki/Hyperventilation" title="Hyperventilation">deep breathing</a> to reduce blood carbon dioxide level to extend the duration of a <a href="/wiki/Free_diving" class="mw-redirect" title="Free diving">free dive</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hyperventilation" title="Hyperventilation">Rapid breathing</a> as the body's response to <a href="/wiki/Hypercapnia" title="Hypercapnia">hypercapnia</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Rapid, often shallow breathing, associated with <a href="/wiki/Panic" title="Panic">panic</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hyperventilation-induced_blackout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hyperventilation-induced blackout</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § underwater blackout syndrome" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#underwater_blackout_syndrome" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">underwater blackout syndrome</a></span></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hypocapnia" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hypocapnia</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hypocapnia" title="Hypocapnia">Hypocapnia</a></span></p>
Abnormally low tissue and blood carbon dioxide concentration.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hypothermia" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hypothermia</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hypothermia" title="Hypothermia">Hypothermia</a></span></p>
A lowering of core body temperature, usually due to heat loss.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hypoxia" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hypoxia</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(medical)" title="Hypoxia (medical)">Hypoxia (medical)</a></span></p>
Abnormally low tissue oxygen concentration: Insufficient oxygen in the body to support normal activities or consciousness.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hypoxic_training" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hypoxic training</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">prolonged underwater distance swimming or extended breath-hold intervals.<sup id="cite_ref-Boyd_et_al_2015_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyd_et_al_2015-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="I">I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>


<dt class="glossary" id="iaogp" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">IAOGP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#international_Association_of_Oil_and_Gas_Producers"><span title="See entry on this page at § International Association of Oil and Gas Producers" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">International Association of Oil and Gas Producers</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="icd" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ICD</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#isobaric_counterdiffusion"><span title="See entry on this page at § isobaric counterdiffusion" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">isobaric counterdiffusion</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="idrcf" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">IDRCF</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="idrf" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">IDRF</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/International_Diving_Regulators_and_Certifiers_Forum" title="International Diving Regulators and Certifiers Forum">International Diving Regulators and Certifiers Forum</a>, previously International Diving Regulators Forum. A voluntary group of diving regulators and certifying agencies formed to work together toward mutual recognition and to identify and implement best practices in diver training with the object of harmonizing cross border diver training standards outside Europe. Members include Australia, Canada, France, Norway, South Africa and United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2010b_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2010b-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="idsa" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">IDSA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/International_Diving_Schools_Association" title="International Diving Schools Association">International Diving Schools Association</a>: Formed with the primary purpose of developing common internationional diving standards for all occupational divers, Offshore, Inshore and Inland, and specialist related non-diving qualifications e.g. Supervisor, DMT and LST.<sup id="cite_ref-IDSA_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDSA-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="imca" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">IMCA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/International_Marine_Contractors_Association" title="International Marine Contractors Association">International Marine Contractors Association</a>.</span></p>
International trade association for the marine contracting industry.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inert_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">inert gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Inert_gas_uptake_(Ingassing)" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Inert gas uptake (Ingassing)</a></span></p>
A gas which is not metabolically active, used to dilute the breathing gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ingassing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ingassing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Inert_gas_uptake_(Ingassing)" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Inert gas uptake (Ingassing)</a></span></p>
Inert gas uptake in body tissues during a dive or other hyperbaric exposure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inherent_unsaturation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">inherent unsaturation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Inherent_unsaturation" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Inherent unsaturation</a></span></p>
Metabolic reduction of total gas pressure in the tissues.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inshore_diver" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">inshore diver</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Colloquial term for a diver who works on inland dive sites or coastal waters not associated with the oil and gas industry. Also referred to as "civils" as much of this work is connected with civil engineering works.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="integrated_weight_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">integrated weight system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any system for carrying dive weights on the buoyancy compensator or diving safety harness, avoiding the use of a separate weight harness or weightbelt.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="internal_condition_of_cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">internal condition of cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The state of the internal surface of a cylinder regarding corrosion, contamination and cracking.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="interstitial_emphysema" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">interstitial emphysema</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Gas trapped in the spaces between organs after lung <a href="/wiki/Barotrauma" title="Barotrauma">barotrauma</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="international_association_of_oil_and_gas_producers" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">International Association of Oil and Gas Producers</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Oil_and_Gas_Producers" class="mw-redirect" title="International Association of Oil and Gas Producers">International Association of Oil and Gas Producers</a></span></p>
The international forum of the oil and gas producing industry.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inverter_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">inverter line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § tripping line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#tripping_line" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">tripping line</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="in-water_recompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">in-water recompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/In-water_recompression" title="In-water recompression">In-water recompression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyperbaric_treatment_schedules#In-water_recompression_schedules" title="Hyperbaric treatment schedules">Hyperbaric treatment schedules#In-water recompression schedules</a></span></p>
Recompression of a diver by returning to a specified depth in the water, followed by decompression on a specified gas, commonly oxygen, as treatment for decompression sickness or as prophylaxis for incomplete or missed decompression after a dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">IP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Intermediate Pressure, or Interstage Pressure. The reduced pressure between the first and second stages of a diving regulator. Also referred to as LP (Low Pressure) in this context.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="isobaric_blackout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">isobaric blackout</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § constant depth blackout" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#constant_depth_blackout" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">constant depth blackout</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="isobaric_counterdiffusion" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">isobaric counterdiffusion</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Isobaric_counterdiffusion" title="Isobaric counterdiffusion">Isobaric counterdiffusion</a></span></p>
The diffusion of gases in opposite directions caused by a change in the composition of the external ambient gas or breathing gas without change in the ambient pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="isolation_manifold" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">isolation manifold</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Connection between two scuba cylinders which when open allows free flow of gas in both directions between the cylinders, but has an isolation valve to block this flow.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="isolation_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">isolation valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">valve in an isolation manifold (q.v.) used to close the gas passage through the manifold and isolate the contents of the two cylinders. Used to prevent a leak on one cylinder from causing the other cylinder to also lose gas.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J">J</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: J">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ja">Ja</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ja">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="jackstay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jackstay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Jackstay#Diving_jackstay" title="Jackstay">Jackstay#Diving jackstay</a></span></p>
A line secured at both ends to serve as a support<sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_Jackstay_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_Jackstay-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> or guide.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jackstay_search" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jackstay search</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See:<a href="/wiki/Underwater_searches#Jackstay_search" title="Underwater searches">Underwater searches#Jackstay search</a></span></p>
Underwater search techniques using one or more jackstays to guide the searcher.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jack-up_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jack-up rig</dfn></dt>
