<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jackup_rig" title="Jackup rig">Jackup rig</a></span></p>
A type of mobile platform that consists of a buoyant hull fitted with a number of movable legs, capable of raising its hull over the surface of sea. The buoyant hull enables transportation of the unit and all attached machinery to a desired location. Once on location the hull is raised to the required elevation above the sea surface on its legs supported by the sea bed.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="j-cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">J-cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Bulk gas storage cylinder with internal volume 50 litres.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Je">Je</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Je">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="jersey_upline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Jersey upline</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § upline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#upline" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">upline</a></span></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ji">Ji</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ji">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="jic_fitting" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">JIC fitting</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/JIC_fitting" title="JIC fitting">JIC fitting</a></span></p>
A type of pipe and hose fitting with a 37-degree flare seating surface. Commonly used in umbilical hose connections.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jim_suit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">JIM suit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/JIM_suit" title="JIM suit">JIM suit</a></span></p>
An atmospheric diving suit manufactured by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Underwater_Marine_Equipment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Underwater Marine Equipment (page does not exist)">Underwater Marine Equipment</a> Limited.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jo">Jo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Jo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="jocking_strap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jocking strap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">webbing strap system used with diving helmets to hold the helmet assembly down on the diver to prevent buoyancy lifting it when underwater.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jonline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Jonline</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jonline" class="mw-redirect" title="Jonline">Jonline</a></span></p>
A short line used to connect to a shotline or anchor line, allowing the diver to move a short horizontal distance away to decompress. The line helps compensate for vertical movement in the anchor line or shot line due to waves.<sup id="cite_ref-shipwreckexpo_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shipwreckexpo-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="job_safety_analysis" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">job safety analysis</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="jsa" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">JSA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Job_safety_analysis" title="Job safety analysis">Job safety analysis</a></span></p>
A procedure to integrate health and safety principles and practices into a particular task or job. Each basic step of the job analysed to identify potential hazards and controls for each hazard.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="j-search" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">J-search</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Underwater_searches#Variations_on_the_jackstay_search" title="Underwater searches">Underwater searches#Variations on the jackstay search</a></span></p>
A variation on the movable jackstay search suitable for a single diver.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Je_2">Je</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Je">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="jump" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jump</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A path from a main guideline to another which is not in contact</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jump_camera" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jump camera</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A camera mounted on a frame, which when lowered to the bottom of a body of water, takes a photograph, usually of the bottom under the camera. The frame constrains the camera to a fixed camera to subject distance, resulting in photographs of uniformly sized areas of bottom, equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Quadrat" title="Quadrat">quadrats</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jump_jacket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Jump jacket</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Harness_with_buoyancy_compensation" title="Surface-supplied diving">harness</a> with integral buoyancy jacket specifically designed for commercial diving work with helmets and bells.<sup id="cite_ref-Jump_Jacket_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jump_Jacket-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jump_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jump line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Cave_diving" title="Cave diving">Cave diving</a></span></p>
A short <span title="See entry on this page at § " class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">error: non-alphabetic term</span> used to connect between two permanent lines that are not in contact. May also be used to search for the other end of a break in a cave line and repair the break</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jump_reel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jump reel</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="jump_spool" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">jump spool</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A reel or spool with a relatively short line intended to be used as a jump line (q.v.).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="j-valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">J-valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Reserve_valves" title="Scuba cylinder valve">Scuba cylinder valve#Reserve valves</a></span></p>
Scuba cylinder valve with lever operated reserve mechanism.<sup id="cite_ref-Basic_Scuba_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Basic_Scuba-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="K">K</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: K">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>


<dt class="glossary" id="kayak_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">kayak diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kayak_diving" class="mw-redirect" title="Kayak diving">Kayak diving</a></span></p>
Diving from a special purpose kayak used to get to the site where the distance from a suitable entry and exit point is inconvenient for shore diving.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="k-cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">K-cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Bulk high pressure gas storage cylinder size designation (approximately 50 litres internal volume)</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kelly" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Kelly</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="kelly_tube" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">Kelly tube</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#tube"><span title="See entry on this page at § tube" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">tube</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="k-valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">K-valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Plain_valves" title="Scuba cylinder valve">Scuba cylinder valve#Plain valves</a></span></p>
Scuba cylinder valve without reserve mechanism.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="L">L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="La">La</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: La">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="lanyard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lanyard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lanyard" title="Lanyard">Lanyard</a></span></p>
A piece of cordage used to secure or lower things; usually it is used where there is a risk of losing the object</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lars" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LARS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#launch_and_Recovery_System"><span title="See entry on this page at § Launch and Recovery System" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Launch and Recovery System</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="laryngospasm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">laryngospasm</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Laryngospasm" title="Laryngospasm">Laryngospasm</a></span></p>
An uncontrolled or involuntary muscular contraction (spasm) of the laryngeal cords which causes a partial blocking of breathing in, while breathing out remains easier.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="latent_hypoxia" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">latent hypoxia</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">While freediving, an arterial oxygen partial pressure which is sufficient to sustain consciousness at depth, but when ascending drops to hyoxic levels due to the reduction of ambient pressure, associated with <a href="/wiki/Freediving_blackout#Blackout_on_ascent" title="Freediving blackout">ascent blackout</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="launch_and_recovery_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">launch and recovery system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Mechanised system for lowering a diving bell, diving stage, submersible or ROV from a vessel, offshore platform, dockside or other platform, and lifting it back on board.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lay_barge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lay barge</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: <b>pipelay barge</b></span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Pipe-laying_ship" title="Pipe-laying ship">Pipe-laying ship</a> and <a href="/wiki/Submarine_pipeline" title="Submarine pipeline">Submarine pipeline</a></span></p>
Barge on which pipeline sections are assembled, welded and laid on the seabed as the barge is moved forward.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lay_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lay line</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="laying_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">laying line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Cave_diving#Line_management" title="Cave diving">Cave diving#Line management</a></span></p>
To run line (unreel under light tension while advancing) and <a href="#placement"><span title="See entry on this page at § placement" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">place it</span></a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lazy_shot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lazy shot</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_shot#Lazy_shot" title="Diving shot">Diving shot#Lazy shot</a></span></p>
A <span title="See entry on this page at § shot line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#shot_line" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">shot line</a></span> (q.v.) which does not reach the bottom</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lds" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LDS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Local dive shop. A retailer of recreational diving equipment, which may also sell cylinder fills, service equipment, provide training or book or organise recreational dives for customers.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Le">Le</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Le">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="led" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LED</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Light_emitting_diode" class="mw-redirect" title="Light emitting diode">Light emitting diode</a></span></p> 
A semiconductor device for producing light from an electrical current commonly used in dive lights.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lens_port" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lens port</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary">Transparent window on an <a href="/wiki/Underwater_camera_housing" class="mw-redirect" title="Underwater camera housing">underwater camera housing</a> through which light reaches the lens.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Li">Li</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Li">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="lid" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LID</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#low_impact_diving"><span title="See entry on this page at § low impact diving" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">low impact diving</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="lifeline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lifeline</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Lifeline_(diving)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lifeline (diving)">Lifeline (diving)</a></span></p>
A line connected securely to the diver at one end and anchored at the other end at the diving control point, which is handled by a line tender, and is used to <a href="/wiki/Diver_communications#Rope_signals" title="Diver communications">communicate</a> with the diver and provide a means of finding the diver for a surface standby diver, and for assisting the diver to the surface and back to the control point if necessary.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="life_support" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">life support</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="life_support_system" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">life support system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Life-support_system#Underwater_and_saturation_diving_habitats" title="Life-support system">Life-support system#Underwater and saturation diving habitats</a></span></p>
Equipment vital to the short term survival of the diver. Most notably the <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">breathing gas</a> supply, and for <a href="/wiki/Saturation_diving" title="Saturation diving">saturation diving</a>, equipment for providing a correctly pressurised environment. In some cases thermoregulatory equipment is also considered life support, and in saturation diving, all of the peripheral systems essential to maintaining a habitable saturation system.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="life_support_package" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">life support package (LSP)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "fly-away package"</span></p>
A collection of equipment and supplies kept in a suitable location such that when a hyperbaric rescue chamber or self-propelled hyperbaric lifeboat arrives at the safe haven it is available to support or complete decompression by using the LSP components to maintain the decompression environment by way of power, gas mixtures, heating and cooling.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="life_support_supervisor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">life support supervisor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A senior life support technician (q.v.) appointed by the diving contractor to supervise the operation of saturation life-support systems.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="life_support_technician" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">life support technician</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "LST"</span></p>
A person who operates and maintains the life support systems of a saturation diving system.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lift_bag" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lift bag</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="lifting_bag" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">lifting bag</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lifting_bag" title="Lifting bag">Lifting bag</a></span></p>
A robust and air-tight bag with straps, which is used to lift heavy objects underwater by means of the bag's buoyancy when filled with air.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="light" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">light</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Alternative term for a <span title="See entry on this page at § viewport" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#viewport" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">viewport</a></span> of a <span title="See entry on this page at § standard diving helmet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#standard_diving_helmet" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">standard diving helmet</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="light_head" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">light head</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The part of a <span title="See entry on this page at § canister light" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#canister_light" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">canister light</a></span> (q.v.) which emits light, and is held in the hand or mounted on the helmet.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lightweight_helmet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lightweight helmet</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_helmet#Lightweight_demand_helmets" title="Diving helmet">Diving helmet#Lightweight demand helmets</a></span></p>
Low volume, close fitting diving helmet, usually with demand valve. Neutrally buoyant, and moves with the diver's head.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="line_marker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">line marker</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Line_arrows" class="mw-redirect" title="Line arrows">Line arrows</a>, <span title="See entry on this page at § cookies" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#cookies" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">cookies</a></span> and sometimes clothes pegs. Tags used to indicate the direction to an exit, midway point between exits, jumps and personal markers to identify divers on a guide line in an <a href="#overhead_environment"><span title="See entry on this page at § overhead environment" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">overhead environment</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="line_tender" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">line tender</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § diver&#39;s attendant" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diver&#39;s_attendant" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diver's attendant</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="line_trap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">line trap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Narrow gap where the guide line passes but divers can not get through.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lipid_pneumonia" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lipid pneumonia</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lipid_pneumonia" title="Lipid pneumonia">Lipid pneumonia</a></span></p>
A lung inflammation (pneumonia) that develops when lipids enter the bronchial tree</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="live-aboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">live-aboard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Liveaboard" title="Liveaboard">Liveaboard</a></span></p>
A large boat which provides transport, accommodation and services for vacationing recreational divers</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="live-boating" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">live-boating</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Diving from a boat which is under way (not moored). The major implication is that the engines will be running and propellers or thrusters may be engaged while divers are in the water, a significant hazard.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(offshore diving) Diving from a vessel underway, making way, but not using dynamic positioning. In offshore diving, diving from a DPV is not considered live-boating.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lo">Lo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Lo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="lock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lock</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "air-lock", "airlock" and "air lock"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Airlock" title="Airlock">Airlock</a></span></p>
Compartment of a hyperbaric habitat or chamber which can be entered through two or more openings which can be closed and sealed, and the pressure adjusted relative to the adjacent chambers. Used to transfer personnel or equipment between areas of different pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lock-in" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lock-in</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Enter a pressurised environment through an <a href="/wiki/Airlock" title="Airlock">airlock</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lock-off" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lock-off</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Disconnect a mobile hyperbaric chamber from another hyperbaric chamber after sealing the doors between them and venting the connection space.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lock-off_time" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lock-off time</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The time at which a diving bell under pressure is locked off (disconnected) from the compression chamber(s) on deck.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lock-on" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lock-on</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Connect a mobile hyperbaric chamber to another hyperbaric chamber so that the pressures can be equalised to allow <a href="/wiki/Transfer_under_pressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Transfer under pressure">transfer under pressure</a> between them.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lock-on_time" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Lock-on time</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The time at which a diving bell under pressure is locked on (reconnected) ready for equalisation to the compression chamber(s) on deck.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lock-out" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lock-out</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Exit from a pressurised environment through an air-lock</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lockout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lockout</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Lockout%E2%80%93tagout" title="Lockout–tagout">Lockout–tagout</a></span></p>
Safety procedure when working on a hazardous energy source.<sup id="cite_ref-OSHA_Lockout_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSHA_Lockout-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lockout_mode" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lockout mode</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dive_computer#Lockout_mode" title="Dive computer">Dive computer#Lockout mode</a></span></p> 
Factory set function of some dive computers which disables the computer from decompression calculation after a violation of a factory set limit for depth, decompression ceiling or other violation of approved operating range for a period sufficient for tissues to fully desaturate if the diver survives uninjured. Some models will lockout immediately, usually to gauge mode which provides depth and time data but no decompression information, leaving the diver without some safety-critical information, others will continue to provide the diver with best estimate decompression information until the end of the dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="log_book" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">log book</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Record of dives kept as proof of experience. Optional for recreational divers, but legally required for professional divers in many jurisdictions.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="long_hose" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">long hose</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">5 ft to 7 ft interstage hose used on one of the regulators used by cave and other technical divers, which allows gas sharing through narrow spaces where the divers must pass through in single file.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="longshore_current" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">longshore current</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Longshore_current" class="mw-redirect" title="Longshore current">Longshore current</a></span></p>
Mass transport of water along a shoreline, often due to wave action at an angle to the shoreline.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "breathing loop"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Concentric_bellows_counterlungs" title="Rebreather">Rebreather#Concentric bellows counterlungs</a></span></p>
The circuit in a rebreather through which the breathing gas passes during a breathing cycle.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loop_mix" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loop mix</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="loop_mixture" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">loop mixture</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The breathing gas in the loop of a rebreather.</dd> 
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Composition of the breathing gas in the loop of a rebreather, usually after passing through the scrubber, where it is analysed for oxygen partial pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loop_volume" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loop volume</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Volume of the breathing loop of a rebreather.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loop_vent_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loop vent valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An over-pressure relief valve in a rebreather loop.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lost_buddy_drill" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lost buddy drill</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="lost_buddy_procedure" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">lost buddy procedure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">standardised procedure followed when a diver realises that their buddy is not where they should be. Procedures may vary depending on the circumstances and training organisations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lost_line_drill" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lost line drill</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="lost_line_procedure" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">lost line procedure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Standardised procedure to be followed when the guideline to the surface is lost in a penetration dive, often in conditions of low visibility and darkness.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="low_impact_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">low impact diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Low_impact_diving" title="Low impact diving">Low impact diving</a></span></p>
Diving with low environmental impact. Diving in a way that avoids contact with or disturbance of sensitive organisms and adversely affecting the environment. Usually applied to recreational diving.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="low_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">low pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Also: "intermediate pressure"<br />
In diving, low pressure usually refers to the gas pressure provided from the first stage regulator to the demand valve for reduction to ambient pressure, the pressure provided by a low-pressure breathing air compressor to the gas panel for supply to the diver's umbilical or airline, or the pressure supplied to buoyancy compensator, dry suit or supply for lift bag inflation gas or pneumatic tools. These pressures are generally less than 30 bar, and in the case of scuba regulators are usually about 9 to 11 bar above ambient pressure.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In the context of diving cylinders, in the US, a low pressure cylinder has a working pressure below 2,500 pounds per square inch (170&#160;bar)</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="low_visibility" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">low visibility</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="low_viz" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">low viz</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Underwater_vision#Low_visibility" title="Underwater vision">Underwater vision#Low visibility</a></span></p>
Water where, regardless of illumination, the distance over which objects can be seen is small. It is a term with highly variable and often relative meaning, but it would be almost universally accepted that less than 0.5 metres (1.6&#160;ft) visibility would be considered low visibility. For operational purposes NOAA define it as "When visual contact with the dive buddy can no longer be maintained", and DAN Southern Africa  suggest less than 3 metres (9.8&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Christou_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christou-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_Low_visibility_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_Low_visibility-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lp" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#low_pressure"><span title="See entry on this page at § low pressure" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">low pressure</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="lp_compressor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LP compressor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Low-pressure compressor. Used for breathing air supply for surface supplied air diving.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lp_cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LP cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Low-pressure cylinder (US) with working pressure less than 2,500 pounds per square inch (170&#160;bar).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lp_port" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LP port</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Opening on the first stage of a regulator through which regulated gas is supplied at low/intermediate pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lst" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">LST</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#life_support_technician"><span title="See entry on this page at § life support technician" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">life support technician</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lu">Lu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Lu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="lung_packing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lung packing</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="lung-packing" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">lung-packing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § glossopharangeal insufflation" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#glossopharangeal_insufflation" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">glossopharangeal insufflation</a></span></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="M">M</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: M">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ma">Ma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="mammalian_diving_reflex" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mammalian diving reflex</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "diving response"</span></p>
A reflex response to breathhold and chilling of the face diving response expressed by the cardiovascular system, which exhibits hypertension, bradycardia, oxygen conservation, arrhythmias, and contraction of the spleen.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindholm_and_Lundgren_2009_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindholm_and_Lundgren_2009-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="manifold" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">manifold</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § twin cylinder manifold" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#twin_cylinder_manifold" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">twin cylinder manifold</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="manifold_(breathing_gas_supply)" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">manifold (breathing gas supply)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "<a href="/wiki/Gas_panel" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas panel">gas panel</a>"</span></p>
Panel for the distribution of diver breathing gas.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="manifold_operator" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">manifold operator</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "gas man"</span></p>
A person such as a life support technician (LST), diving supervisor, or mixed-gas diver, who is designated to perform the duties of gas distribution on a surface-supplied mixed gas (HeO<sub>2</sub>) diving operation, who is competent in the operation of the manifold and whose primary responsibility is to operate the manifold.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="manual_bypass_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">manual bypass valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A valve that allows the diver to manually inject gas into the breathing loop of a rebreather, bypassing the valve operated by the control system.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="manual_closed_circuit_rebreather" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">manual closed circuit rebreather</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "mCCR", "MCCR". See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § diver controlled closed circuit rebreather" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diver_controlled_closed_circuit_rebreather" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diver controlled closed circuit rebreather</a></span></span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Closed_circuit_mixed_gas_rebreathers" title="Rebreather">Rebreather#Closed circuit mixed gas rebreathers</a></span></p>
A closed circuit rebreather which relies on the diver to monitor and control the gas mixture in the loop.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="manufacturing_standard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">manufacturing standard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "manufacturing code"</span></p>
Set of design and manufacturing rules intended to produce uniform and safe products by several manufacturers in an industry.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="marsh_marine_connector" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Marsh Marine connector</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of the popular underwater plug connector systems for diver communications cables.<sup id="cite_ref-Marsh_Marine_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marsh_Marine-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="martini&#39;s_law" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Martini's law</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Rough rule of thumb for estimating <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis" title="Nitrogen narcosis">nitrogen narcosis</a> effects based on equivalence to consumption of <a href="/wiki/Dry_martini" class="mw-redirect" title="Dry martini">dry martinis</a>: Variously quoted as one martini per 10&#160;m or one martini per 50&#160;ft depth.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="master_link" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">master link</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(<a href="/wiki/Rigging_(material_handling)" title="Rigging (material handling)">Rigging</a>): The large heavy duty link to which the legs of a <a href="/wiki/Chain_sling" class="mw-redirect" title="Chain sling">chain sling</a> are attached, and which is the attachment point on the sling for the lifting hook or shackle</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="maze_cave" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">maze cave</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Cave structure characterised by multiple branches and changes in direction.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mccr" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mCCR</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="mccr" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">MCCR</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#manual_closed_circuit_rebreather"><span title="See entry on this page at § manual closed circuit rebreather" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">manual closed circuit rebreather</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Me">Me</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Me">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="metres_sea_water" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">metres sea water</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Metres_sea_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Metres sea water">metres sea water</a></span></p>
Unit of pressure equal to 1/10 bar. Not a linear measure of depth.<sup id="cite_ref-NORSOK_U100_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NORSOK_U100-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mi">Mi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Mi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="microbubbles" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">microbubbles</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Microscopic bubbles which are not detectable by ultrasound or Doppler ultrasound, yet can affect the likelihood of DCS by slowing off-gassing.<sup id="cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="micronuclei" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">micronuclei</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Microscopic cavities that function as bubble seeds by absorbing dissolved gas.<sup id="cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mid-water" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mid-water</dfn></dt> 
<dt class="glossary" id="midwater" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">midwater</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Significantly distant from both the bottom and the surface.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="medical_lock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">medical lock</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Small <a href="#lock"><span title="See entry on this page at § lock" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lock</span></a> on a decompression chamber used for transfer of medical equipment and other supplies into and out of the chamber while the chamber remains under pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mix" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mix</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Short for <a href="/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)" title="Trimix (breathing gas)">trimix</a> breathing gas</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mixed_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mixed gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">Breathing gas</a> for diving other than air, but usually implies a helium based mixture.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mixed_mode_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mixed mode diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A mixed mode dive team is a buddy team where the divers use different modes of diving on the same dive, such as one diver on open circuit and the other on rebreather<sup id="cite_ref-Seymour_2016_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seymour_2016-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></dd> 

<dt class="glossary" id="mixed_platform_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mixed platform diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Mixed platform rebreather diving refers to the use of different makes or models of rebreather on the same dive.<sup id="cite_ref-Seymour_2016_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seymour_2016-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mo">Mo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Mo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="mobile_diving_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mobile diving system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "portable diving system"</span></p>
A <span title="See entry on this page at § diving system" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_system" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diving system</a></span> (q.v.) which is installed on a vessel or installation on a temporary basis and that is not fixed, i.e. can be demobilised, transported and re-sited. Includes surface supplied air, nitrox, heliox and saturation diving systems.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mobile_offshore_drilling_unit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mobile offshore drilling unit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A generic term for several classes of self-contained floatable or floating drilling rigs such as drilling vessels, semisubmersibles, submersibles, jack-ups, and similar facilities that can be moved without substantial effort. These facilities may have self-propulsion equipment on board and may require dynamic positioning equipment or mooring systems to maintain their position.<sup id="cite_ref-MODU_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MODU-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mod" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">MOD</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Maximum_operating_depth" title="Maximum operating depth">Maximum operating depth</a>:  Limiting depth for safety based on <a href="/wiki/Partial_pressure" title="Partial pressure">partial pressure</a> of oxygen of a breathing gas mixture.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="modified_flutter_kick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">modified flutter kick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Version of the <span title="See entry on this page at § flutter kick" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#flutter_kick" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">flutter kick</a></span> finning style which reduces risk of silting by directing thrust more directly backwards. Two techniques exist: One version has the legs bent at the knees so that the fins are placed relatively high and on average are aligned more horizontally. The other version has one fin stationary below the moving fin to deflect downwash.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Leg movement is restrained, and ankle movement used for precision manoeuvring.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="modified_frog_kick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">modified frog kick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Version of the <span title="See entry on this page at § frog kick" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#frog_kick" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">frog kick</a></span> finning style which reduces risk of silting by directing thrust more directly backwards. Performed with bent knees and fins raised above the line of the torso.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="modu" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">MODU</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#mobile_offshore_drilling_unit"><span title="See entry on this page at § mobile offshore drilling unit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">mobile offshore drilling unit</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="monofin" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">monofin</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Monofin" title="Monofin">Monofin</a></span></p>
A type of swimfin typically used in finswimming and free-diving. It consists of a single surface attached to footpockets for both of the diver's feet.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="molecular_sieve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">molecular sieve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Molecular_sieve" title="Molecular sieve">Molecular sieve</a></span></p>
Material containing tiny pores of a precise and uniform size that is used as an adsorbent for gases and liquids. Molecules small enough to pass through the pores are absorbed while larger molecules are not. It is different from a common filter in that it operates on a molecular level.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="monkey_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">monkey diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Terminology" title="Sidemount diving">Sidemount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
The use of <span title="See entry on this page at § sidemount" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#sidemount" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">sidemount</a></span> configuration and procedures with a single cylinder.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="moonpool" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">moonpool</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moonpool" class="mw-redirect" title="Moonpool">Moonpool</a></span></p>
An opening in the floor or base of the hull, platform, underwater habitat, or chamber, giving access to the water below.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="msw" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">msw</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#metres_sea_water"><span title="See entry on this page at § metres sea water" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">metres sea water</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mu">Mu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Mu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="multi-level_dive" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">multi-level dive</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "multilevel dive", "multi level dive"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Multi-level_dive" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-level dive">Multi-level dive</a></span></p>
A <a href="/wiki/Dive_profile" title="Dive profile">dive profile</a> in which the diver remains in more than one distinct depth ranges (excluding decompression stops) for a significant period before beginning final ascent to the surface.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="multiple_stage_compressor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">multiple stage compressor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Compressor#Reciprocating_compressors" title="Compressor">Compressor#Reciprocating compressors</a></span></p>
Compressor in which gases are compressed more than once, usually with cooling between stages. Used to improve efficiency and reduce temperatures.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mung" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mung</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A brown organic deposit usually found on the ceilings of caves which is easily dislodged by diver's exhaust bubbles and then drifts down through the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="mushroom_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">mushroom valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A rubber non-return valve flap which is circular or oval, with a stem in the middle to attach it to the holder in the centre of the grating over the orifice.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="m-value" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">M-value</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#M-values" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#M-values</a></span></p>
At a given ambient pressure, the M-value is the maximum theoretical value of absolute inert gas pressure that a tissue compartment can take without presenting symptoms of decompression sickness.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="N">N</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: N">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Na">Na</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Na">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="nacd" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">NACD</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/National_Association_for_Cave_Diving" title="National Association for Cave Diving">National Association for Cave Diving</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="narcs" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">narcs</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#nitrogen_narcosis"><span title="See entry on this page at § nitrogen narcosis" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">nitrogen narcosis</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="navy_experimental_diving_unit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Navy Experimental Diving Unit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Navy_Experimental_Diving_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Navy Experimental Diving Unit">Navy Experimental Diving Unit</a></span></p> 
The United States Navy Experimental Diving Unit, the primary source of diving and hyperbaric operational guidance for the US Navy, located in Florida</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="navy_seal" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Navy SEAL</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/U.S._Navy_Seals" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Navy Seals">U.S. Navy Seals</a></span></p>
A US Navy trained combat diver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ndl" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">NDL</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#no_decompression_limit"><span title="See entry on this page at § No decompression limit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">No decompression limit</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ne">Ne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="neck_dam" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">neck dam</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The lower part of a <a href="/wiki/Diving_helmet#Lightweight_demand_helmets" title="Diving helmet">lightweight diving helmet</a> which includes a neoprene or latex neck seal similar to the neck seal on a dry suit, to prevent ingress of water. The alternative is to clamp the helmet to the diver's <a href="/wiki/Drysuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Drysuit">drysuit</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="necklace" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">necklace</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Bungee loop attached to the secondary regulator second stage, worn around the neck to store the secondary close under the chin, where it is protected and the diver is immediately aware of a free-flow. With a little adjustment and practice it is possible to pick it up by head and mouth movement alone, not needing use of a hand. The bungee is attached to the second stage by a breakaway connection, often a close-fitting loop over the mouthpiece, so that it can be moved away from the diver's head in an emergency without disturbing the primary second stage or the mask.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="neck_thread" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">neck thread</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Cylinder_neck" title="Diving cylinder">Diving cylinder#Cylinder neck</a></span></p>
Internal screw thread in the bore of the <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#cylinder_neck" title="Diving cylinder">cylinder neck</a> to fit a <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#The_cylinder_valve" title="Diving cylinder">cylinder valve</a>, which controls flow of gas into and out of the cylinder.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nedu" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">NEDU</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#navy_Experimental_Diving_Unit"><span title="See entry on this page at § Navy Experimental Diving Unit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Navy Experimental Diving Unit</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="negative_buoyancy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">negative buoyancy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: just "negative" in context</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also <span title="See entry on this page at § diving heavy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_heavy" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diving heavy</a></span></span></p> 
Buoyancy less than weight. Insufficient upward force due to buoyancy to keep afloat or remain at constant depth</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="negative_buoyancy_entry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">negative buoyancy entry</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="negatively_buoyant_entry" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">negatively buoyant entry</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="negative_entry" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">negative entry</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries_and_exits" title="Scuba skills">Scuba skills#Entries and exits</a></span></p>
Entry into the water in a buoyancy condition that will sink by default. When intentional, generally after reducing buoyancy of BC and, if applicable, dry suit by venting to ensure that the diver will not float back to the surface, but will continue to descend.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="negative_pressure_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">negative pressure breathing</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="negative_static_lung_load" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">negative static lung load</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Human_physiology_of_underwater_diving#Positive_and_negative_pressure_breathing" title="Human physiology of underwater diving">Human physiology of underwater diving#Positive and negative pressure breathing</a></span></p>
Breathing against an external pressure slightly less than the relaxed pressure in the lungs. More effort is needed to inhale, less to exhale. This can occur when using back mounted counterlungs on a rebreather, in a steep head up position with a single-hose demand valve, or when snorkelling.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="neo-haldanian" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">neo-Haldanian</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "neo-Haldanean"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Critical_difference_hypothesis" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Critical difference hypothesis</a></span></p>
Decompression models based on later modifications of the principles described by <a href="/wiki/John_Scott_Haldane" title="John Scott Haldane">John Scott Haldane</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="neoprene" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">neoprene</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Neoprene" title="Neoprene">Neoprene</a></span></p>
Synthetic elastomer used in the form of foamed sheets as the material for most <a href="/wiki/Wetsuit" title="Wetsuit">wetsuits</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Drysuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Drysuit">drysuits</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="neutral_buoyancy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">neutral buoyancy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Buoyancy" title="Buoyancy">Buoyancy</a></span></p>
Having a fully immersed buoyancy exactly equal to weight, so that the forces are balanced and the person or object statically remains at a constant depth. Effectively average density is equal to that of the surrounding fluid medium. The state of neutral buoyancy is typically <a href="/wiki/Metastable" class="mw-redirect" title="Metastable">metastable</a> for a compressible system.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="newtsuit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Newtsuit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Newtsuit" title="Newtsuit">Newtsuit</a></span></p>
An <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_diving_suit" title="Atmospheric diving suit">atmospheric diving suit</a> designed and originally built by <a href="/wiki/Phil_Nuytten" title="Phil Nuytten">Phil Nuytten</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="net_cutter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">net cutter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A handle with a hooked blade used to cut netting or cordage to free the diver from entanglement</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nfci" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">NFCI</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Non-freezing_cold_injury" title="Non-freezing cold injury">Non-freezing cold injury</a>: Permanent tissue damage due to low temperature exposure without any freezing damage.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ni">Ni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="niggles" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">niggles</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness#Signs_and_symptoms" title="Decompression sickness">Decompression sickness#Signs and symptoms</a></span></p>
Minor symptoms characteristic of mild decompression sickness.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="night_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">night diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Night_diving" title="Night diving">Night diving</a></span></p>
Diving during the hours of darkness.</dd>
