<dt class="glossary" id="nimh" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">NiMH</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Nickel-metal_hydride" class="mw-redirect" title="Nickel-metal hydride">Nickel-metal hydride</a>. A technology for <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery" title="Rechargeable battery">rechargeable battery</a> cells.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nitrile" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">nitrile</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nitrile_rubber" title="Nitrile rubber">Nitrile rubber</a></span></p>
A synthetic <a href="/wiki/Elastomer" title="Elastomer">elastomer</a> used for most standard <a href="/wiki/O-ring" title="O-ring">O-ring</a> seals.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nitrogen" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">nitrogen</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">Nitrogen</a></span></p>
The major component gas of air and many <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">breathing gas</a> mixtures used in diving. Important in diving as an active agent in <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis" title="Nitrogen narcosis">nitrogen narcosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nitrogen_narcosis" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">nitrogen narcosis</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis" title="Nitrogen narcosis">Nitrogen narcosis</a></span></p>
Also known as narcs, inert gas narcosis, raptures of the deep, Martini effect: A reversible alteration in consciousness that occurs while breathing gases containing nitrogen under elevated partial pressure similar to alcohol intoxication or nitrous oxide inhalation, and can occur during shallow dives, but usually does not become noticeable until greater depths, beyond 30 meters.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nitrox" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">nitrox</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "Enriched Air Nitrox (EAN)"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Nitrox" title="Nitrox">Nitrox</a></span></p>
Mixture of nitrogen and oxygen for use as breathing gas. Usually with oxygen percentage higher than air.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nitrox_stick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">nitrox stick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving#Mixing_the_gases" title="Gas blending for scuba diving">Gas blending for scuba diving#Mixing the gases</a></span></p>
A mixing tube used to blend oxygen with air before compressing to make nitrox breathing gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="noaa" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">NOAA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (US)</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="no_decompression_limit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">no decompression limit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#No_decompression_limit" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#No decompression limit</a></span></p>
No decompression limit. The maximum time which a diver can remain at a specified depth without incurring a stage decompression obligation in terms of the specified decompression tables or algorithm.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nominal_capacity" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">nominal capacity</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Volume of <span title="See entry on this page at § free gas volume" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#free_gas_volume" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">free gas</a></span> contained by a scuba cylinder when filled to <span title="See entry on this page at § charging pressure" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#charging_pressure" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">charging pressure</a></span> at constant temperature.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="no-mount_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">No-mount diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Side_mount_diving#Terminology" class="mw-redirect" title="Side mount diving">Side mount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
A specialized overhead-environment strategy for dealing with particularly tight restrictions which may involve divers wearing a very basic harness or simply hand-carrying cylinders.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="normoxic" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">normoxic</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A breathing gas mixture with oxygen content approximating atmospheric air.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A breathing gas for diving which contains sufficient oxygen to minimise risk of hypoxia at atmospheric pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nss" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">NSS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/National_Speleological_Society" title="National Speleological Society">National Speleological Society</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="nystagmus" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">nystagmus</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nystagmus" title="Nystagmus">Nystagmus</a></span></p>
An oscillation of the eyes alternating a slow eye movement in one direction, and a fast eye movement in the other direction.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="O">O</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: O">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>


<dt class="glossary" id="octopus_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">octopus breathing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Sharing air using an octopus regulator</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="octopus_regulator" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">octopus regulator</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "octo reg", "safe second"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator#Octopus" title="Diving regulator">Diving regulator#Octopus</a></span></p>
A secondary demand valve fitted to a diving first stage for use as an alternative air source for another diver in case of an emergency. Also occasionally useful as a backup in case of some kinds of malfunction of the primary</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="offboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">offboard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Not an integral part of the scuba unit. Usually applied to gas cylinders carried additional to the <a href="#onboard_gas"><span title="See entry on this page at § onboard gas" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">onboard gas</span></a> of a rebreather.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="offboard_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">offboard gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Gas carried in cylinders not integrally mounted on a rebreather, but plumbed into the unit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="off-gassing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">off-gassing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#outgassing"><span title="See entry on this page at § outgassing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">outgassing</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="offshore" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">offshore</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A significant distance away to seaward from the shoreline.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Outside the national maritime border, in international waters, though generally still inside the exclusive economic zone.<sup id="cite_ref-Offshore_ACOP_2014_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Offshore_ACOP_2014-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="offshore_diver" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">offshore diver</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Commercial_offshore_diving" title="Commercial offshore diving">Commercial offshore diving</a></span></p> 
Colloquial term for a diver who works in the offshore oil and gas industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> A professional diver who works in regions outside the jurisdiction of national occupational health and safety and labour laws.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="o-lay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">O-lay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Method for installation of sub-sea pipeline for the oil and gas industry. The pipe is constructed in an onshore construction yard, moved into the water and bent into a spiral without causing plastic deformation of the material. When the pipeline is sufficiently long it is transported with the help of tugs to the installation area. At the installation area the pipeline is unwound and pulled over a simple lay barge with stinger and installed on the bottom.<sup id="cite_ref-O-lay_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O-lay-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oled" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">OLED</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main: <a href="/wiki/OLED" title="OLED">OLED</a></span></p>
Organic light-emitting diode: A low energy high contrast light source commonly used on instrument displays such as later generation dive computers.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="omitted_decompression_procedure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">omitted decompression procedure</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="omitted_decompression_protocol" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">omitted decompression protocol</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Procedure for managing a diver who surfaces without completing required decompression. If a chamber is available, the diver is recompressed in it, otherwise if no symptoms have presented, the diver may be recompressed as soon as practicable in the water. Various schedules for further decompression depend on the dive history.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="onboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">onboard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Mounted directly onto the unit as an integral component. Usually applied to gas cylinders mounted on a rebreather frame or housing, or emergency gas supply cylinders mounted on a diving bell or stage.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="onboard_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">onboard gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Gas carried in cylinders mounted as part of a unit, usually a rebreather or diving bell or stage.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="on-gassing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">on-gassing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § ingassing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#ingassing" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">ingassing</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="onshore" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">onshore</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § inshore" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#inshore" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">inshore</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="open_circuit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">open circuit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Breathing apparatus which discharges exhaled gas into the environment, without any further use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="open_water" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">open water</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href="/wiki/List_of_diving_environments_by_type#Environments_by_confinement" title="List of diving environments by type">List of diving environments by type#Environments by confinement</a></i>. 
Water where there is no physical obstruction to a direct ascent to the surface.<sup id="cite_ref-open_water_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-open_water-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Water which is open to influences by weather and climatic conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Class_IV_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Class_IV-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="optode" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">optode</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="optrode" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">optrode</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Optode" title="Optode">Optode</a></span></p>
Optical sensor device to measure a specific substance, usually with the aid of a chemical transducer.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ooa" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">OOA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Out of air. An emergency situation where the supply of breathing gas to the diver has stopped.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="opv" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">OPV</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Over-pressure valve. A <a href="/wiki/Pressure_relief_valve" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressure relief valve">pressure relief valve</a> which automatically opens at a set pressure to allow excess gas to escape.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="o-ring" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">O-ring</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/O-ring" title="O-ring">O-ring</a></span></p>
A mechanical gasket in the shape of a torus; a loop of elastomer with a circular cross-section, designed to be seated in a groove and compressed during assembly between two or more parts, creating a seal at the contact surfaces.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oro-nasal_mask" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oro-nasal mask</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="ori-nasal_mask" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">ori-nasal mask</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary">A breathing mask that covers the mouth and nose only. It may be an independent item, such as an oxygen mask or <span title="See entry on this page at § BIBS" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#BIBS" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">BIBS</a></span> mask, or it may be a component inside a full face diving mask or helmet to reduce the amount of <a href="/wiki/Dead_space_(physiology)" title="Dead space (physiology)">dead space</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="otu" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">OTU</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#oxygen_toxicity_unit"><span title="See entry on this page at § oxygen toxicity unit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">oxygen toxicity unit</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="outgassing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">outgassing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Outgassing_of_tissues" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Outgassing of tissues</a></span></p>
Diffusion of gas out of the tissue into the blood, and transport to the lungs where it diffuses into the lung gas and is eliminated by exhalation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="overhead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">overhead</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A physical or procedural obstruction to a direct ascent to the surface. Physical overheads include cave, cavern or culvert ceilings, fishing nets, ship hulls, and wreckage. Procedural overheads are generally a decompression obligation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="overrun" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">overrun</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Excessive rotation of a reel or spool by inertia, causing the line to unwind beyond the amount paid out, and lie in loose coils on the spool which can jam or tangle.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="overweighting" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">overweighting</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § diving heavy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_heavy" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diving heavy</a></span></span></p>
Carrying more ballast weight than is necessary to achieve neutral buoyancy at all times during a dive. In scuba diving usually a dangerous error, but used in surface-supplied diving to stabilise the diver when working on the bottom.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">Oxygen</a></span></p>
Important component gas of <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_air" class="mw-redirect" title="Atmospheric air">atmospheric air</a> and essential component of any <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">breathing gas</a>. Required to sustain life.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_analyser" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen analyser</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_analyzer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen analyzer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_analyzer" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxygen analyzer">Oxygen analyzer</a></span></p>
Instrument for measuring the partial pressure of oxygen in a gas mixture</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_cell" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen cell</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Electro-galvanic_oxygen_sensor" title="Electro-galvanic oxygen sensor">Electro-galvanic oxygen sensor</a> for measuring partial pressure of oxygen in the breathing gas using an oxygen analyser</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_clean" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen clean</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility#Oxygen_cleaning" title="Oxygen compatibility">Oxygen compatibility#Oxygen cleaning</a></span></p>
Cleaned for <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxygen service">oxygen service</a> by appropriate methods and materials and tested for contaminants. Verified that particulates, fibres, oils, greases and other contaminants are absent.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_clock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen clock</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_toxicity#Underwater" title="Oxygen toxicity">Oxygen toxicity#Underwater</a></span></p>
A notional alarm clock, which accumulates hyperbaric oxygen exposure at a rate which increases with higher oxygen partial pressure toward the maximum single exposure limit recommended. This <a href="/wiki/Dive_computer#Display_information" title="Dive computer">function is implemented</a> as cumulative oxygen exposure for acute (CNS) oxygen toxicity in some dive computers.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_compatible" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen compatible</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility" title="Oxygen compatibility">Oxygen compatibility</a></span></p>
Made from materials which are suitable for oxygen service. Capable of coexisting with elevated oxygen concentrations and a potential source of ignition without flashing, based on a system’s maximum operating pressure and temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_compatible_air" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen compatible air</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Air which has been filtered to reduce contaminants to a level suitable for blending with high pressure oxygen. Air with a reduced level of condensable hydrocarbon mist or vapour.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_design" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen design</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_service_design" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen service design</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility#Oxygen_service_design" title="Oxygen compatibility">Oxygen compatibility#Oxygen service design</a></span></p> 
Design that minimizes any tendency for heat generation, ignition of particulates, or the accumulation of contaminants for an intended partial pressure of oxygen and temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_fraction" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen fraction</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas#Classification_by_oxygen_fraction" title="Breathing gas">Breathing gas#Classification by oxygen fraction</a></span></p>
Fraction by volume or pressure of the gas mixture made up by oxygen</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_pete" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Oxygen Pete</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Imaginary monster associated with <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_toxicity#History" title="Oxygen toxicity">CNS oxygen toxicity</a>, also a CNS oxygen toxicity seizure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_rebreather" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen rebreather</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Oxygen_rebreathers" title="Rebreather">Rebreather#Oxygen rebreathers</a></span></p>
A <span title="See entry on this page at § closed circuit rebreather" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#closed_circuit_rebreather" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">closed circuit rebreather</a></span> that uses only oxygen as a gas supply.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_sensor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen sensor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A component that produces a signal in response to the presence or concentration of oxygen. In diving this is usually a galvanic cell that generates a current and voltage proportional to the partial pressure of oxygen in a breathing gas.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_service" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen service</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See:<a href="/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility#Oxygen_service" title="Oxygen compatibility">Oxygen compatibility#Oxygen service</a></span></p> 
Suitable for operating with significantly higher levels of oxygen than normal atmospheric air. Often implies special cleaning procedures, use of oxygen compatible materials, and design to reduce ignition risk. System or component that has been designed and tested for oxygen use, has been tested as oxygen clean and is oxygen compatible.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_toxicity" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen toxicity</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_toxicity" title="Oxygen toxicity">Oxygen toxicity</a></span></p>
A condition resulting from the harmful effects of breathing molecular oxygen (O<sub>2</sub>) at elevated partial pressures.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_toxicity_unit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen toxicity unit</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary">Unit of exposure to toxic concentrations of oxygen in breathing gas, primarily in connection with pulmonary oxygen toxicity and oxidative damage to cell membranes. The accumulation of OTUs depends on time and partial pressure of exposure, and dissipation is a function of recovery time at non-toxic partial pressures.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="oxygen_window" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">oxygen window</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_window_in_diving_decompression" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxygen window in diving decompression">Oxygen window in diving decompression</a></span></p>
Inherent unsaturation due to metabolic reduction of total gas pressure in the tissues.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="panic" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">panic</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Panic" title="Panic">Panic</a></span></p>
A sudden sensation of fear which is so strong as to dominate or prevent reason and logical thinking, replacing it with overwhelming feelings of anxiety and frantic agitation consistent with an animalistic fight-or-flight reaction</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="parallel_compartments" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">parallel compartments</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Perfusion_limited_tissues_and_parallel_tissue_models" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Perfusion limited tissues and parallel tissue models</a></span></p>
A decompression model comprising a group of tissues with varied rates of perfusion, but supplied by blood of approximately equivalent gas concentration. It is assumed that there is no gas transfer between tissue compartments by diffusion. This results in a parallel set of independent tissues, each with its own rate of ingassing and outgassing dependent on the rate of blood flowing through the tissue</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="partial_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">partial pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Partial_pressure" title="Partial pressure">Partial pressure</a></span></p>
(Abbreviation PP or pp) The pressure that a component gas of a gas mixture would exert if it alone was present in the volume occupied by the gas mixture.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="passive_addition" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">passive addition</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Passive_addition_semi-closed_circuit" title="Rebreather">Rebreather#Passive addition semi-closed circuit</a></span></p>
Feed gas addition system for semi-closed circuit rebreathers which discharges a part of the gas in the breathing circuit. fresh gas is added when the volume of the circuit decreases during inhalation and triggers the addition valve. Compare with <span title="See entry on this page at § active addition" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#active_addition" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">active addition</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="patent_foramen_ovale" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">patent foramen ovale</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Patent_foramen_ovale" class="mw-redirect" title="Patent foramen ovale">patent foramen ovale</a></span></p>
A common form of congenital heart defect that enables blood flow between the left and right atria through a gap in the interatrial septum. In some circumstances this may increase risk of decompression sickness if venous blood carrying gas bubbles is shunted into the arterial system, bypassing the pulmonary capillary network filter.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pe">Pe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="pendulum_rebreather" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pendulum rebreather</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "push-pull rebreather"</span></p>
Rebreather with a single breathing hose from the mouthpiece to the scrubber and counterlung. Gas passes through it in both directions, unlike the one-way <span title="See entry on this page at § breathing loop" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#breathing_loop" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">breathing loop</a></span> configuration. The volume of the hose between the mouthpiece and scrubber is <a href="/wiki/Dead_space_(physiology)#In_breathing_apparatus" title="Dead space (physiology)">dead space</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="penetration" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">penetration</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Penetration_diving" class="mw-redirect" title="Penetration diving">Penetration diving</a></span></p>
Entering a region with no direct vertical access to the surface, such as a cave or the interior of a wreck.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="penetration_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">penetration line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § distance line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#distance_line" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">distance line</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="percolation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">percolation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Cave diving: Bubbles making their way to the walls and the ceiling of the cave and dislodging silt.<sup id="cite_ref-x-ray_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-x-ray-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="perfusion" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">perfusion</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Perfusion" title="Perfusion">Perfusion</a></span></p>
The process of delivery of blood to a capillary bed in the biological tissue.<sup id="cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="perfusion_limited" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">perfusion limited</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Deterministic_models" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Deterministic models</a></span></p>
The assumption in a decompression model that perfusion has the dominant influence on gas uptake and release. Compare with <span title="See entry on this page at § diffusion limited" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diffusion_limited" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diffusion limited</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="permanent_stamp_markings" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">permanent stamp markings</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="permanent_markings" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">permanent markings</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="stamp_markings" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">stamp markings</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Permanent_stamp_markings" title="Diving cylinder">Diving cylinder#Permanent stamp markings</a></span></p>
Text stamped into the metal of the shoulder of a diving cylinder providing obligatory and optional information about the cylinder.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="personal_locator_beacon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">personal locator beacon</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "PLB"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Emergency_locator_beacon" title="Emergency locator beacon">Emergency locator beacon</a></span></p>
Radio beacons for personal use which are intended to indicate a person in distress who is away from normal emergency services.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="personal_safety_equipment" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">personal safety equipment</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Personal_protective_equipment" title="Personal protective equipment">Personal protective equipment</a></span></p>
Equipment worn by personnel to reduce risk of injury at sites where it is not practicable to eliminate the hazard, including ear protectors, safety glasses, hard hats, gloves, overalls, respirators etc. Diving suits and underwater breathing apparatus are also personal protective equipment.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pfo" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">PFO</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#patent_foramen_ovale"><span title="See entry on this page at § patent foramen ovale" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">patent foramen ovale</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="photo_quadrat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">photo quadrat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § jump camera" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#jump_camera" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">jump camera</a></span></span></p>
A photograph of a <a href="/wiki/Quadrat" title="Quadrat">quadrat</a> taken for later analysis. Common in marine ecological research where in situ counting would be impractical. Quadrats may be identified by rigid frames or by a fixed camera to subject distance.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pi">Pi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="pig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pig</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Pigging#Pipeline_Inspection_Gauge" title="Pigging">Pigging#Pipeline Inspection Gauge</a></span></p>
Pipeline inspection gauge: A tool that is sent through a pipeline and propelled by the pressure of the product in the pipeline itself, for purposes such as cleaning, dewatering, inspecting, measuring, separation of contents, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pigtail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pigtail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Coiled section of pipe to provide greater flexibility.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pillar_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pillar valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <span title="See entry on this page at § cylinder valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#cylinder_valve" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">cylinder valve</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="pin_index_connection" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pin index connection</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pin_Index_Safety_System" title="Pin Index Safety System">Pin Index Safety System</a></span></p>
Standard connection type for portable medical oxygen cylinder valves and regulators.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pipeline_end_manifold" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pipeline end manifold</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "PLEM"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Pipeline_end_manifold" class="mw-redirect" title="Pipeline end manifold">Pipeline end manifold</a></span></p>
The place where a flexible underwater hose string is attached to connect a seabed pipeline with a single point mooring.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="piston_bolt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">piston bolt</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § bolt snap" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bolt_snap" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bolt snap</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="placement" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">placement</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Securing the <span title="See entry on this page at § guideline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#guideline" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">guideline</a></span> as it is being run.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The choice of primary and secondary tie offs of the guideline.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="plb" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">PLB</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="#personal_locator_beacon"><span title="See entry on this page at § personal locator beacon" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">personal locator beacon</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="plem" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">PLEM</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#pipeline_end_manifold"><span title="See entry on this page at § pipeline end manifold" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">pipeline end manifold</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="pneumo_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pneumo breathing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving_skills#Breathing_from_a_pneumofathometer_hose" title="Surface-supplied diving skills">Surface-supplied diving skills#Breathing from a pneumofathometer hose</a></span></p>
Use of the pneumofathometer hose to supply breathing gas to a surface supplied diver in an emergency. Supply can be from the diver's own pneumo hose or from a standby diver's pneumo hose.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pneumofathometer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pneumofathometer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "pneumo", "Kluge-Pneumo"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Pneumofathometer" class="mw-redirect" title="Pneumofathometer">Pneumofathometer</a></span></p>
Instrument to measure the depth of a diver, which measures the ambient pressure at the diver by measuring the pressure in a hose filled with air with an open end at the diver and with the surface end connected to a gas supply, control valve and pressure gauge calibrated in msw, fsw, or often both.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pneumothorax" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pneumothorax</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pneumothorax" title="Pneumothorax">Pneumothorax</a></span></p>
Air or other breathing gas in the chest cavity, outside of the lung, particularly between the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_pleurae" title="Pulmonary pleurae">pulmonary pleurae</a>, sometimes resulting in a collapsed lung.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Po">Po</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Po">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="pony_cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pony cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pony_cylinder" class="mw-redirect" title="Pony cylinder">pony cylinder</a></span></p>
Relatively small scuba set carried as an independent alternative breathing gas source by a scuba diver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="p-port" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">P-port</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large bore quick connector fitting designed and used by Draeger on diving and firefighting breathing apparatus, which has been used in rebreathers, particularly modifications.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="positive_displacement" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">positive displacement</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(of compressor) A configuration that compresses gas by reducing the volume of the compression chamber (eg. cylinder) by mechanical means (eg. piston) to produce higher pressure of the contents which flow out via the exhaust valve.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="positive_pressure_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">positive pressure breathing</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="positive_static_lung_load" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">positive static lung load</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Human_physiology_of_underwater_diving#Positive_and_negative_pressure_breathing" title="Human physiology of underwater diving">Human physiology of underwater diving#Positive and negative pressure breathing</a></span></p>
Breathing against an external pressure slightly greater than the relaxed pressure in the lungs. More effort is needed to exhale, less to inhale. This can occur when using a positive pressure mask, front mounted counterlungs on a rebreather, or if in a steep head down position with a single-hose demand valve.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="positive_pressure_mask" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">positive pressure mask</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A full-face mask which maintains an internal pressure slightly higher than external ambient pressure, necessitating slight positive pressure breathing, and ensuring that if the mask skirt seal fails, gas will leak out, rather than water leaking in, which provides a more secure airway and provides some protection against contaminated water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pre-fill_external_inspection" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pre-fill external inspection</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Examination of the external condition of a pressure vessel and fittings to ensure that it complies with requirements before accepting for filling.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pre-mix" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pre-mix</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Nitrox blend with high oxygen content used to mix nitrox by topping up the decanted pre-mix with air.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pressure_gradient" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pressure gradient</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The rate of change of partial pressure of dissolved gas through a solvent, which is the driving mechanism for diffusion through the solvent. Also loosely used to refer to the difference between the dissolved gas pressure in a tissue and ambient pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pressure_transducer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pressure transducer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: pressure sensor</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main: <a href="/wiki/Pressure_transducer" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressure transducer">Pressure transducer</a></span></p>
A component that produces a signal proportional to a pressure input, which can be processed to give an output indicating the pressure. Used in dive computers, electronic pressure gauges, and pressure transmitters, among other uses.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pressure_transmitter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pressure transmitter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: wireless pressure transmitter</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Pressure_transmitter" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressure transmitter">pressure transmitter</a></span></p>
Pressure transducer (q.v.) with a wireless transmitter that sends a coded signal to the diver's dive computer which uses the data to display remaining cylinder pressure, which can in some applications be used to provide other gas management information.</dd> 

<dt class="glossary" id="primary_light" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">primary light</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The main light to be used on a dive. Usually the most powerful.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="primary_regulator" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">primary regulator</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">the regulator which the diver intends to breathe from for most of the dive. Particularly when diving with back-mounted manifolded twin cylinders.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="primary_tie-off" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">primary tie-off</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">First tie off of the guideline in a penetration dive. This is usually made in a place with free vertical access to the surface.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="professional_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">professional diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Professional_diving" title="Professional diving">Professional diving</a></span></p>
Diving which is done as part of the diver's employment or professional occupation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="progressive_penetration" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">progressive penetration</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An incremental approach to cave and wreck exploration. Each dive goes a bit further so that the divers develop a familiarity with the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="prv" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">PRV</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Pressure_relief_valve" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressure relief valve">Pressure relief valve</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="psi" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">psi</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Pounds_per_square_inch" class="mw-redirect" title="Pounds per square inch">Pounds per square inch</a>. <a href="/wiki/Unit_of_measurement" title="Unit of measurement">Unit</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">pressure</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial system">Imperial system</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ptt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">PTT</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Push to talk: Voice communication systems which require the user to press a button to transmit. Used with through water systems to conserve battery power.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pu">Pu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="public_safety_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">public safety diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_safety_diving" title="Public safety diving">public safety diving</a></span></p>
The underwater work conducted by law enforcement, fire department rescue, and search &amp; rescue/recovery dive teams.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pull" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pull</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A relatively long pull on a lifeline when used for <a href="/wiki/Diver_communications#Commercial_diving_rope_signals" title="Diver communications">rope signals</a>. (see "bell" for comparison).</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Part of an ascent between the bottom and a decompression stop, between decompression stops, or to the surface. Possibly deriving from the practice of pulling a surface supplied diver up by the umbilical or lifeline.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pulmonary_over-inflation_syndrome" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">pulmonary over-inflation syndrome</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Barotrauma" title="Barotrauma">Barotrauma</a></span></p>
Pulmonary barotrauma of ascent. Lung over-pressure injury.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="purge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">purge</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To press the purge button on a demand valve to induce a gas flow which is intended to clear the demand valve interior of water or other substances.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="purge_button" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">purge button</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Button or flexible area on the front or side of a demand valve which allows the user to manually open the second stage valve to provide gas flow without inhalation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="purge_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">purge valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Non-return valve in snorkel or mask which allows water to drain either under gravity or as a result of exhalation into the air space</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="push_gradient" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">push gradient</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Tech diving jargon: Decompress at a high gradient factor, particularly when exceeding the baseline M-value. This will expose the diver to a higher risk of developing decompression sickness while reducing time decompressing in the water.<sup id="cite_ref-Watts_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watts-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="push-pull_rebreather" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">push-pull rebreather</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#pendulum_rebreather"><span title="See entry on this page at § pendulum rebreather" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">pendulum rebreather</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="p-valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">P-valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "Pee-valve"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dry_suit#The_P-valve" title="Dry suit">Dry suit#The P-valve</a></span></p>
A valved catheter fitted to a dry suit, which enables a diver to urinate at any time without having to get out of the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="pyle_stops" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Pyle stops</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Pyle_stops" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Pyle stops</a></span></p>
Named after <a href="/wiki/Richard_Pyle" title="Richard Pyle">Richard Pyle</a>, an early advocate of deep stops. An additional brief deep decompression stop, typically 2 minutes long and half way between the maximum depth and the first conventional decompression stop.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Q">Q</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Q">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>


<dt class="glossary" id="quick_link" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">quick link</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Oval connector shaped like a chain link with a screw gate on one side.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="quad" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">quad</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A group of high pressure gas storage cylinders mounted upright on a frame and manifolded together. Usually in 4, 6, 9, 12, or 16 cylinder arrangements.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="quadrat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">quadrat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Quadrat" title="Quadrat">Quadrat</a></span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="#photo_quadrat"><span title="See entry on this page at § photo quadrat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">photo quadrat</span></a></span></p>
A small, typically rectangular plot used in ecology and geography to isolate a standard unit of area for study of the distribution of an item over a large area. The quadrat is suitable for sampling plants and slow-moving or sessile animals.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="R">R</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: R">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ra">Ra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="rams_head" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">rams head</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "cobra guard", <span title="See entry on this page at § valve cage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#valve_cage" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">valve cage</a></span></span></p>
Frame attached to the top of back-mounted scuba cylinders to protect valves, manifold, and regulator first stages from impact with the surroundings.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rapture_of_the_deep" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">rapture of the deep</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § nitrogen narcosis" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#nitrogen_narcosis" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">nitrogen narcosis</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="rash_guard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">rash guard</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="rash_vest" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">rash vest</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="rashie" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">rashie</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rash_guard" title="Rash guard">rash guard</a></span></p> 
A shirt made of spandex and nylon or polyester, worn to protect against rashes caused by abrasion, and jellyfish stings. These shirts can be worn by themselves, in tropical water, or under a wetsuit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rat_hat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Rat hat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Ratcliffe diving helmet, Designed by Bob Ratcliffe, later produced by Oceaneering International. No longer in production.<sup id="cite_ref-Rat_hat_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rat_hat-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ratio_decompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ratio decompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "ratio deco"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ratio_decompression" title="Ratio decompression">Ratio decompression</a></span></p>
A technique for calculating decompression schedules for scuba divers engaged in deep diving without using dive tables, decompression software or a dive computer.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis_2011_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis_2011-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Powell_2012_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powell_2012-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rdp" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">RDP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#recreational_Dive_Planner"><span title="See entry on this page at § Recreational Dive Planner" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Recreational Dive Planner</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Re">Re</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Re">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="rebreather" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">rebreather</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_rebreather" title="Diving rebreather">Diving rebreather</a></span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § gas extender" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#gas_extender" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">gas extender</a></span> and <a href="#reclaim_system"><span title="See entry on this page at § reclaim system" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">reclaim system</span></a></span></p> 
<a href="/wiki/Underwater_breathing_apparatus" title="Underwater breathing apparatus">Underwater breathing apparatus</a> which recycles most of the exhaled gas, removing carbon dioxide and topping up oxygen before the gas is breathed again.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reciprocating_compressor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reciprocating compressor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reciprocating_compressor" title="Reciprocating compressor">Reciprocating compressor</a></span></p>
Compressor in which the volume of the compression chamber/s is cyclically changed by reversing linear motion. E.g.: a piston moving back and forth in a cylinder.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reclaim_helmet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reclaim helmet</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Saturation_diving" title="Saturation diving">Saturation diving</a></span></p>
Diving helmet with a reclaim gas regulator allowing exhaled gas to be safely returned to the surface through an additional hose on the umbilical.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reclaim_regulator" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reclaim regulator</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Reclaim_regulator" class="mw-redirect" title="Reclaim regulator">Reclaim regulator</a></span></p>
A diving regulator designed to safely return exhaled gas to a reclaim hose at lower than ambient pressure. Function is similar to a <span title="See entry on this page at § BIBS" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#BIBS" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">BIBS</a></span> exhaust valve.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reclaim_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reclaim system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Saturation_diving" title="Saturation diving">Saturation diving</a></span></p>
System for recovering helium based breathing gas used by divers and recycling it.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="recompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">recompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Subjecting a diver to pressure after an ascent from a dive as treatment for <a href="/wiki/Decompression_illness" title="Decompression illness">decompression illness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Preferably done in a <a href="/wiki/Recompression_chamber" class="mw-redirect" title="Recompression chamber">recompression chamber</a>, but occasionally done as <a href="/wiki/In-water_recompression" title="In-water recompression">in-water recompression</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Returning a diver to pressure as the first stage of <span title="See entry on this page at § surface decompression" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#surface_decompression" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">surface decompression</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § omitted decompression procedure" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#omitted_decompression_procedure" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">omitted decompression procedure</a></span> to prevent <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a> from developing.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="recompression_chamber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">recompression chamber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Recompression_chamber" class="mw-redirect" title="Recompression chamber">Recompression chamber</a></span></p>
