A hyperbaric chamber used to treat divers suffering from certain <a href="/wiki/Diving_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Diving disorder">diving disorders</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="recovery_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">recovery breathing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "hook breathing"</span></p></dd>
<dd class="glossary">A technique used by freedivers on surfacing to reduce the risk of surface blackout. A partial exhalation is made, followed by a quick inhalation, then the diver closes the airway and pressurises for a few seconds as if about to cough. This is repeated a few times over the first 30 seconds or so on the surface. The aim is to keep thoracic pressure slightly raised to artificially raise arterial oxygen partial pressure or prevent it from dropping in the critical seconds until newly oxygenated blood can reach the brain, and thereby prevent surface blackout. This is the same technique used by pilots during high-g maneuvers, and by mountaineers at high altitude.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="recreational_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">recreational diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Recreational_diving" title="Recreational diving">Recreational diving</a></span></p>
Recreational diving or sport diving is a type of diving that uses scuba equipment for the purpose of leisure and enjoyment. In some diving circles, the term "recreational diving" is used in contradistinction to "<span title="See entry on this page at § technical diving" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#technical_diving" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">technical diving</a></span>", a more demanding aspect of the sport which requires greater levels of training, experience and equipment. In other circles, technical diving is considered a subset of recreational diving as opposed to "<a href="#professional_diving"><span title="See entry on this page at § professional diving" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">professional diving</span></a>", which is done as part of the diver's work.</dd>

<span class="anchor" id="recreational_Dive_Planner"></span>
<dt class="glossary" id="recreational_dive_planner" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Recreational Dive Planner</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "RDP"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Recreational_Dive_Planner" title="Recreational Dive Planner">Recreational Dive Planner</a></span></p>
A no-stop decompression table developed by DSAT.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="red_tide" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">red tide</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § algal bloom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#algal_bloom" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">algal bloom</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="reduced_gradient_bubble_model" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reduced gradient bubble model</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reduced_gradient_bubble_model" title="Reduced gradient bubble model">Reduced gradient bubble model</a></span></p>
A computationally intensive bubble model decompression algorithm developed by Bruce Wienke.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="redundancy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">redundancy</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="redundant" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">redundant</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Engineering_redundancy" class="mw-redirect" title="Engineering redundancy">Engineering redundancy</a></span></p>
Technical diving philosophy of ensuring that a spare or backup is available for any item of life-support equipment that would immediately endanger the diver if it were to fail.<sup id="cite_ref-Mount_2008b_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mount_2008b-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="redundant_breathing_gas_supply" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">redundant breathing gas supply</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: redundant gas supply, fully redundant gas supply, redundant air supply etc.</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Redundant_breathing_gas_supply" class="mw-redirect" title="Redundant breathing gas supply">Redundant breathing gas supply</a></span></p>
A breathing gas supply, carried by the diver, which is both suitable for the depths at which it may be breathed, and sufficient to allow the diver to make a safe and controlled return to the surface or other place where more breathing gas is available, which is not used during the dive, and is stored in one or more cylinders which are mot the one the diver is breathing from at any given time.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="redundant_equipment" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">redundant equipment</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">duplicated or spare equipment carried by the diver or team to substitute for vital primary equipment in case of a malfunction. In some cases, such as cave lights, multiple redundancy may be desirable. A redundant breathing gas supply is the most common example.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Mechanism used to store, deploy and recover long lengths of line at low tension.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reference_temperature" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reference temperature</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Temperature at which a cylinder may be safely and legally filled to the nominal <span title="See entry on this page at § charging pressure" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#charging_pressure" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">charging pressure</a></span> without corrections.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="regulator" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">regulator</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A <a href="/wiki/Pressure_regulator" title="Pressure regulator">mechanism</a> for controlling the output pressure of a high pressure gas supply.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;As 1, <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator" title="Diving regulator">with a demand valve</a> (q.v.) incorporated which provides the diver with breathing gas at ambient pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="regulator_changeout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">regulator changeout</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="regulator_swap-out" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">regulator swap-out</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary">Scuba emergency skill of swapping a correctly functioning regulator with one that is malfunctioning to gain access to breathing gas in a cylinder while underwater. Usually applied to side- or sling-mounted cylinders.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="regulator_freeze" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">regulator freeze</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Ice_diving#Regulator_freezing" title="Ice diving">Ice diving#Regulator freezing</a></span></p>
Locking of the regulator mechanism caused by freezing of the water due to expansion cooling of the regulated air. Often causes the mechanism to lock open, causing free flow and further cooling.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reject_criteria" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reject criteria</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="rejection_criteria" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">rejection criteria</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Features, states or conditions which are not acceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="repetitive_dives" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">repetitive dives</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Repetitive_dives" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Repetitive dives</a></span></p>
Any dive which is done while the tissues retain residual inert gas from a previous dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="repet-up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">repet-up</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Commercial diving term for a type of multilevel dive, in which the depth is decreased over elapsed time, with the purpose of allowing a longer useful dive time and minimising decompression time.<sup id="cite_ref-Overland_1999_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overland_1999-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="repex" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Repex</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Method of estimating tolerable repetitive exposure to high partial pressure oxygen.<sup id="cite_ref-Hamilton_1989_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamilton_1989-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rescue_tether" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">rescue tether</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short lanyard or strap carried by a surface supplied stand-by diver to be used to tether an unresponsive diver to the standby diver during a rescue. It is attached at one end to a D-ring on the stand-by diver's harness, and has a clip at the other end which may be secured to a D-ring on the casualty's harness to allow the rescuer the use of both hands during the return to the bell or surface.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reserve_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reserve gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Reserve_pressure" title="Scuba gas planning">Scuba gas planning#Reserve pressure</a></span></p>
Gas which is not intended to be used during the dive, and is reserved for contingencies.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reserve_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reserve valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Cylinder valve with a lever operated bypass valve to release the gas below reserve pressure</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="residual_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">residual gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Gas remaining in a cylinder from the previous fill.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="residual_nitrogen" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">residual nitrogen</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Residual_nitrogen_time" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Residual nitrogen time</a></span></p>
Nitrogen in excess of normal atmospheric saturation remaining in the diver's tissues after a dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="residual_nitrogen_time" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">residual nitrogen time</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "RNT"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Residual_nitrogen_time" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Residual nitrogen time</a></span></p>
Time penalty in a repetitive dive equivalent to time at depth which would produce the residual nitrogen in the diver at the start of the dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="residual_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">residual pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Pressure of the gas remaining in a partly used cylinder from the previous fill.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="respiratory_minute_volume" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">respiratory minute volume</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "minute ventilation"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_minute_volume" class="mw-redirect" title="Respiratory minute volume">Respiratory minute volume</a></span></p> 
The volume of gas inhaled (inhaled minute volume) or exhaled (exhaled minute volume) from a person's lungs in one minute.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="respiratory_quotient" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">respiratory quotient</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_quotient" title="Respiratory quotient">Respiratory quotient</a></span></p>
The ratio of carbon dioxide produced as a metabolic product to the oxygen consumed.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="restriction" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">restriction</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Section of a cave which is difficult to pass through due to lack of space. A minor restriction is too small for two divers to swim through together, a major restriction requires the diver to remove equipment to fit through.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="revalidation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">revalidation</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary">Certification that an item of equipment continues to be fit for service. Usually after passing the required periodic inspection and testing by an approved or authorised practitioner.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reverse_block" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reverse block</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Blockage of a <a href="/wiki/Paranasal_sinuses" title="Paranasal sinuses">sinus</a> or <a href="/wiki/Eustachian_tube" title="Eustachian tube">eustachian tube</a> preventing relatively high internal gas pressure from escaping. <sup id="cite_ref-Dovenbarger_2011_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dovenbarger_2011-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reverse_ear_squeeze" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reverse ear squeeze</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: reverse ear, reverse squeeze, reversed ear.</span></p>
<a href="/wiki/Barotrauma#Ear_barotrauma" title="Barotrauma">Barotrauma of the ear</a> caused by a middle ear gas space pressure greater than ambient pressure, or greater than the pressure in the external autitory canal, causing the eardrum to bulge outwards.<sup id="cite_ref-Dovenbarger_2011_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dovenbarger_2011-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reverse_jump" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reverse jump</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Procedure to cross a <span title="See entry on this page at § gap" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#gap" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">gap</a></span> during an exit which allows the line to be retrieved without returning to the start point. In the event of a line break or removed primary reel, one diver holds the end of the search line at the break point, and the other searches for the other part of the broken line or the exit while laying line from the reel. When the original line or exit is found, the reel handler signals to the static diver with line pulls and the static diver swims in the direction of the line while the reel handler reels it in, recovering the line.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reverse_profile" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reverse profile</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Repetitive dive which is deeper than the previous dive</dd>
<dd class="glossary">Multilevel dive in which a later level is deeper than an earlier level.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="reverse_sinus_squeeze" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">reverse sinus squeeze</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barotrauma" title="Barotrauma">Barotrauma</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Paranasal_sinuses" title="Paranasal sinuses">sinus</a> caused by a relatively high internal pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-Dovenbarger_2011_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dovenbarger_2011-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rgbm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">RGBM</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#reduced_gradient_bubble_model"><span title="See entry on this page at § reduced gradient bubble model" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">reduced gradient bubble model</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ri">Ri</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ri">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="rimbach_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Rimbach system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">System of touch contact signalling used in cave diving. Push forward = go, pull back = back up, squeeze = stop.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ring_bungee" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ring bungee</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § bungee (sidemount)" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bungee_(sidemount)" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bungee (sidemount)</a></span></span></p>
Length of shock cord with metal rings and a clip used to control the position of the top end of a sidemounted cylinder.<sup id="cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Differs from a regular bungee in having the rings.<sup id="cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> A popular configuration is a bolt snap connected to a ring by a quick link, with a length of bungee from the ring to another quick link which is used to connect the assembly to a D-ring on the back of the harness. The bolt snap is clipped to the shoulder D-ring and the cylinder neck bolt snap is clipped to the ring.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rip_current" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">rip current</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Rip_current" title="Rip current">Rip current</a></span></p>
A strong localised flow of water to seaward from near the shore, typically through the surf line</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="riser" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">riser</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Drilling_riser" title="Drilling riser">Drilling riser</a></span></p>
A conduit that provides a temporary extension of a subsea oil well to a surface drilling facility</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rmv" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">RMV</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#respiratory_minute_volume"><span title="See entry on this page at § respiratory minute volume" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">respiratory minute volume</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="rnpl" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">RNPL</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy_Physiological_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Royal Navy Physiological Laboratory (page does not exist)">Royal Navy Physiological Laboratory</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rnt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">RNT</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#residual_nitrogen_time"><span title="See entry on this page at § residual nitrogen time" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">residual nitrogen time</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ro">Ro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="rock_bottom_gas_management" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">rock bottom gas management</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning" title="Scuba gas planning">Scuba gas planning</a></span></p>
Retention of a breathing gas reserve based on calculated values for the amount of gas required for a safe ascent from any point in the planned dive profile. Factors such as emergency supply of gas to a buddy, air consumption rates under stress and decompression gas requirements are considered in the calculations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="roll-off" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">roll-off</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Closing of a cylinder valve as a result of scraping contact between the valve knob and the overhead or other surroundings. The left hand knob is more likely to roll-off, closing the backup regulator in the standard twins configuration. Roll-off is an emergency if the diver does not have an immediately accessible alternative breathable gas supply.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="rov" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ROV</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="rouv" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">ROUV</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Remotely_operated_underwater_vehicle" title="Remotely operated underwater vehicle">Remotely operated underwater vehicle</a>&#160;&#8211; A tethered underwater mobile device operated by a remote crew.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="roughneck" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">roughneck</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Member of the drilling crew who works under the direction of the driller to make or break connections as drillpipe is tripped in or out of the hole.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="roustabout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">roustabout</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any unskilled manual laborer on the rigsite.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ru">Ru</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ru">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="rule_of_thirds" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">rule of thirds</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_thirds_(diving)" title="Rule of thirds (diving)">Rule of thirds (diving)</a></span></p>
<a href="/wiki/Cave_diving" title="Cave diving">Cave</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wreck_diving" title="Wreck diving">wreck</a> penetration breathing gas management convention where no more than one third of the gas in a cylinder may be used on the inward part of the dive, and the other two thirds is kept for exit: One third for the planned exit, and one third in case of an emergency.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="run_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">run line</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="running_line" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">running line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Unreeling line under light tension while advancing. Usually in the context of laying a <a href="/wiki/Distance_line" title="Distance line">distance line</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="run_time" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">run time</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Time elapsed since the start of a dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="running_stop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">running stop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A pause made during ascent to adjust the average ascent rate to the nominal value. For example a nominal ascent rate of 3&#160;m per minute might use an actual ascent rate of about 5&#160;m per minute and make a stop every 3m until the end of the current minute, resulting in a slightly stepped profile with an overall ascent rate corresponding to the nominal rate.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis_2011_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis_2011-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="run_time_schedule" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">run time schedule</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Decompression schedule and dive plan based on elapsed time from the start of the dive, All waypoints and events are specified in terms of elapsed time with start of descent at zero.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="r-valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">R-valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "positive reserve valve", "automatic valve", or "calibrated orifice"</span></p>
A cylinder valve which limits the outflow by a calibrated orifice when in the "on" position.<sup id="cite_ref-Basic_Scuba_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Basic_Scuba-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="S">S</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: S">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sa">Sa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="sac_rate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SAC rate</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#surface_air_consumption_rate"><span title="See entry on this page at § surface air consumption rate" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">surface air consumption rate</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="safe_air" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">safe air</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Term used for <a href="/wiki/Nitrox" title="Nitrox">nitrox</a> by <a href="/wiki/American_Nitrox_Divers_International" title="American Nitrox Divers International">American Nitrox Divers International</a> (ANDI)</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="safe_second" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">safe second</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Obsolete term for <span title="See entry on this page at § octopus regulator" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#octopus_regulator" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">octopus regulator</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="safety-critical_element" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">safety-critical element</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Item of equipment or process with the purpose to prevent or limit the consequences of a high risk hazard, that if realised, could result in the fatality or severe injury of one or more divers or support crew.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="safety_reel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">safety reel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Reel with relatively short line for use in an emergency, usually for searches to find a lost buddy or lost guideline or to jump a line break.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="safety_spool" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">safety spool</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Spool with relatively short line for use in an emergency, usually for searches to find lost buddy or lost guideline or to jump a line break.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="safety_stop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">safety stop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Safety_stop" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Safety stop</a></span></p>
A voluntary (not required by the decompression schedule) additional decompression stop intended to further reduce risk of decompression sickness.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="salt_water_aspiration_syndrome" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">salt water aspiration syndrome</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Salt_water_aspiration_syndrome" title="Salt water aspiration syndrome">Salt water aspiration syndrome</a></span></p>
A reaction of the lungs to inhalation of a mist of salt water</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="samba" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">samba</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Involuntary muscular contractions experienced by breathhold divers when approaching <a href="/wiki/Hypoxic_blackout" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypoxic blackout">hypoxic blackout</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freedivingbiz_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedivingbiz-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sasuba" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Sasuba</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A shallow water recreational airline diving system using a scuba cylinder on a float towed by the diver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="saturation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">saturation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Condition where the inert components of the breathing gas dissolved in a diver's tissues are in equilibrium with the gas in the lungs.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="saturation_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">saturation diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Saturation_diving" title="Saturation diving">Saturation diving</a></span></p>
Diving mode where the divers remain pressurised for periods of several days or weeks and decompress only at the end of the period.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="saturation_diving_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">saturation diving system</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="saturation_spread" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">saturation spread</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Saturation_diving_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Saturation diving system">Saturation diving system</a></span></p>
The combination of equipment and services to operate a saturation diving project. It would include the closed diving bell, the accommodation modules, decompression chamber, life-support systems, gas storage and supply systems, pressurisation equipment, underwater breathing apparatus, and launch and recovery systems. In may also include a hyperbaric evacuation system.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sc">Sc</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sc">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="scba" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SCBA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Self-contained_breathing_apparatus" title="Self-contained breathing apparatus">Self-contained breathing apparatus</a> (not for underwater use).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="schrader_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">schrader valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Schrader_valve" title="Schrader valve">Schrader valve</a></span></p>
Valve using a standard automotive tyre valve insert, common in low pressure inflation hose female connectors and BC inflation valves.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="scientific_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">scientific diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scientific_diving" title="Scientific diving">Scientific diving</a></span></p>
Diving for purposes of scientific research. The rules and constraints of scientific diving vary in different jurisdictions, but generally allow different options to mainstream commercial diving.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="scooter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">scooter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Diver_propulsion_vehicle" title="Diver propulsion vehicle">Diver propulsion vehicle</a> used by scuba divers to increase range underwater.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="scooter_ring" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">scooter ring</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">D-ring on scuba harness used to attach to scooter tow line. Usually on front of the harness crotch strap.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="scr" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SCR</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Semi-closed_circuit_rebreather" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-closed circuit rebreather">Semi-closed circuit rebreather</a>: A rebreather (q.v.) which either dumps part of each breath to the environment or continuously adds gas and dumps the excess. Compare with closed circuit rebreather (CCR) (q.v.).</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Surface Consumption Rate - An alternative term with the same meaning as Surface Air Consumption (SAC) (q.v.). Not to be confused with Semi-closed Circuit Rebreather.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="screw_gate_carabiner" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">screw gate carabiner</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Carabiner" title="Carabiner">Carabiner</a></span></p>
A clip mechanism which can be locked in the closed position by turning a threaded barrel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="scrubber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">scrubber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Carbon_dioxide_scrubber" title="Rebreather">Rebreather#Carbon dioxide scrubber</a></span></p>
Canister containing material (sorb) which chemically combines with carbon dioxide to remove it from the gas passed through the canister.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="scuba" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">scuba</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="scuba" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">SCUBA</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_set" title="Scuba set">Scuba set</a></span></p>
Self-contained underwater breathing apparatus. May be open or closed circuit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="scuba_orienteering" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">scuba orienteering</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_orienteering" class="mw-redirect" title="Scuba orienteering">Scuba orienteering</a></span></p>
Competitive underwater sport in which scuba divers attempt to swim a circuit marked by buoys, without surfacing, using compass navigation and mechanical distance measurement. Points are awarded for time and accuracy according to the specific course definition and length.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="scuba_replacement" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">scuba replacement</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Mobile <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving" title="Surface-supplied diving">surface-supplied diving</a> equipment using portable gas storage cylinders for primary and reserve <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">breathing gas</a> supply. Preferred to scuba for <a href="/wiki/Commercial_diving" title="Commercial diving">commercial diving</a> applications due to lower perceived risk compared to scuba, and because equipment and procedures are otherwise identical to surface supplied diving using compressors for air supply. Used when logistical constraints or air quality issues preclude use of a <a href="/wiki/Diving_air_compressor" title="Diving air compressor">compressor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="s-drill" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">S-drill</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Safety drill. An air sharing exercise based on deploying the long hose primary regulator.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Se">Se</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Se">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="search_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">search line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Underwater_searches" title="Underwater searches">Underwater searches</a></span></p>
Cord used to indicate the transect for a search. The diver moves along the line, searching by sight or feel on one or both sides of the line. After the transect has been searched, the line is moved to the next transect. usually a short distance offset from the previous position, at a distance which depends on the visibility and the size of the target.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="search_pattern" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">search pattern</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Underwater_searches" title="Underwater searches">Underwater searches</a></span></p>
Systematic procedure for covering the search area sufficiently to be reasonably sure of finding a given target if it is there. Several patterns are in general use for underwater searches, depending on the target, the terrain, and available facilities.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="secondary_drowning" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">secondary drowning</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Secondary_drowning" class="mw-redirect" title="Secondary drowning">Secondary drowning</a></span></p>
A complication of aspiration of water or other fluids into the lungs.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="secondary_regulator" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">secondary regulator</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § backup regulator" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#backup_regulator" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">backup regulator</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="second_stage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">second stage</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § demand valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#demand_valve" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">demand valve</a></span></span></p>
The part of a diving regulator which provides pressure reduction from intermediate pressure to ambient pressure on demand. Demand valve.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="self-propelled_hyperbaric_lifeboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">self-propelled hyperbaric lifeboat (SPHL)</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "hyperbaric lifeboat" (HLB), "hyperbaric rescue vessel" (HRV)</span></p>
A pressure vessel adapted for use as a means of hyperbaric evacuation, and fitted to a conventional lifeboat hull.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="semi-dry_suit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">semi-dry suit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_suit#Semi-dry_suit" title="Diving suit">Diving suit#Semi-dry suit</a></span></p>
A wet suit with wrist and ankle seals, and usually a more watertight zipper than usual, to reduce flushing of water through the suit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="separator" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">separator</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vapor%E2%80%93liquid_separator" title="Vapor–liquid separator">Vapor–liquid separator</a></span></p>
Device which facilitates the separation of liquid particles from the compressed gas, usually with a drain to periodically remove accumulated liquid from the system.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="serial_compartments" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">serial compartments</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Diffusion_limited_tissues_and_the_&quot;tissue_slab&quot;,_and_series_models" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Diffusion limited tissues and the "tissue slab", and series models</a></span></p>
A decompression model based on the assumption that diffusion is the limiting mechanism of dissolved gas transport in the tissues, in which there is perfusion transport for one compartment, and diffusion between a series of compartments,</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="serial_number" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">serial number</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main: <a href="/wiki/Serial_number" title="Serial number">Serial number</a></span></p></dd>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Number stamped on the cylinder by the manufacturer in the shoulder area which identifies the cylinder. In combination with the manufacturer’s identification this will be unique to the cylinder.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Character string, including number, marked on an item of equipment by the manufacturer to uniquely identify it.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="setpoint" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">setpoint</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="set-point" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">set-point</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="set_point" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">set point</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rebreather_diving#Set-points" title="Rebreather diving">Rebreather diving#Set-points</a></span></p>
Reference value for oxygen partial pressure in an electronically controlled closed circuit rebreather. The control system monitors the real time value of oxygen partial pressure in the breathing loop and automatically adjusts the composition by adding gas to keep the concentration between the upper and lower set-points.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sgc" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SGC</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="#sAC"><span title="See entry on this page at § SAC" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">SAC</span></a></span></p>
Surface Gas Consumption</dd>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sh">Sh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<dt class="glossary" id="shallow_water_blackout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">shallow water blackout</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Loss of consciousness during a dive associated with occurrence at a shallow depth. Used for several different mechanisms, depending on context, therefore often leading to confusion.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="/wiki/Shallow-water_blackout_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shallow-water blackout (disambiguation)">Shallow-water blackout</a><br />
Loss of consciousness caused by cerebral hypoxia towards the end of a breath-hold dive in water typically shallower than five metres (16 feet), when the swimmer does not necessarily experience an urgent need to breathe and has no other obvious medical condition that might have caused it.<sup id="cite_ref-Boyd_et_al_2015_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyd_et_al_2015-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="/wiki/Freediving_blackout#Terminology" title="Freediving blackout">Freediving blackout#Terminology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latent_hypoxia" title="Latent hypoxia">latent hypoxia</a><br />
Loss of consciousness caused by cerebral hypoxia at the end of a deep breath-hold dive during the latter part of the ascent or immediately after surfacing due to lowered pO<sub>2</sub> caused by reduction in ambient pressure, see also latent hypoxia.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Loss of consciousness while ascending on a rebreather due to sudden drop of pO<sub>2</sub> in the breathing loop, usually associated with manual CCR and SCR.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="shark_pod" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">shark pod</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="shark_shield" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">shark shield</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary">Electrical device carried by a diver intended to repel sharks by electrical field pulses.<sup id="cite_ref-sharkshield_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sharkshield-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="shock_cord" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">shock cord</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Bungee_cord" title="Bungee cord">bungee cord</a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="shore_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">shore diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Diving from a shore entry point.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="shot_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">shot line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_shot" title="Diving shot">Diving shot</a></span></p>
A rope between a float at the surface, and a sufficiently heavy weight holding the rope approximately vertical.<sup id="cite_ref-DR_2001_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DR_2001-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Si">Si</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Si">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dt class="glossary" id="sidemount" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sidemount</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Terminology" title="Sidemount diving">Sidemount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
A scuba diving equipment configuration which has diving cylinders mounted alongside the diver, below the shoulders and along the hips, instead of on the back of the diver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sidemount_staging" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sidemount staging</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Terminology" title="Sidemount diving">Sidemount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
The practice of using sidemount configuration (bungee loops and/or <span title="See entry on this page at § butt-plate" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#butt-plate" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">butt-plate</a></span> rails) as a means for stowing stage/deco cylinders when otherwise diving in <span title="See entry on this page at § backmount" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#backmount" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">back-mounted</a></span> scuba</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="silent_entry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">silent entry</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries" title="Scuba skills">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
An entry technique which minimises noise and splash, suitable for entry from a low platform. The diver sits with feet dangling over or into the water, turns their torso sideways, takes their weight on their hands, then swings off the surface and drops feet first into the water, slowed by their arms, and lets go with the hands when in the water.<sup id="cite_ref-BSAC_Diving_Manual_1982_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSAC_Diving_Manual_1982-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 251">&#58;&#8202;251&#8202;</span></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="silica_gel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">silica gel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Silica_gel" title="Silica gel">Silica gel</a></span></p>
A desiccant filter medium used to adsorb water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="silt_out" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">silt out</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Silt_out" title="Silt out">Silt out</a></span></p>
A situation when underwater visibility is rapidly reduced to zero, usually when a diver disturbs silt deposits.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="silt_screw" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">silt screw</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Cave_diving#Equipment" title="Cave diving">Cave diving#Equipment</a></span></p>
Device which is inserted into silt or sand to provide an anchor point, such as for a tie-off on a cave line.<sup id="cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Silt screws are generally stakes made from small bore plastic (PVC) pipe with a sharpened end.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="simultaneous_operations" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">simultaneous operations</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Two or more potentially clashing operations occurring, for example, at the same time and same location.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="single_point_mooring" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">single point mooring</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Single_buoy_mooring" title="Single buoy mooring">Single buoy mooring</a></span></p>
A loading buoy anchored offshore, that serves as a mooring point and interconnect for tankers loading or offloading gas or liquid products. SPMs are the link between geostatic subsea manifold connections and weathervaning tankers. They are capable of handling any size ship, even very large crude carriers (VLCC) where no alternative facility is available<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sinkhole" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sinkhole</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sinkhole" title="Sinkhole">Sinkhole</a></span></p>
A natural depression or hole in the Earth's surface caused by karst processes — the chemical dissolution of carbonate rocks - or suffosion processes for example in sandstone</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sintered" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sintered</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sintering" title="Sintering">Sintering</a></span></p>
Particulate or granular material bonded together by the application of pressure and sufficient heat to partially melt the surface of the particles and weld them together. The product is usually porous.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="siphon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">siphon</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Place where water from a stream flows into the ground. also "swallow hole"<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="skandalopetra" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">skandalopetra</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Skandalopetra_diving" title="Skandalopetra diving">Skandalopetra diving</a></span></p>
A flat stone, usually of marble or granite, weighing between 8 and 14&#160;kg, with rounded corners and edges, and tied to a rope, historically used by Greek sponge free-divers to assist descent. When the diver wishes to ascend the rope is used to signal the tender on the boat who then pulls in the rope. Currently skandalopetra diving is a competitive sport.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="skin" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">skin</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="skins" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">skins</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § dive skins" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#dive_skins" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">dive skins</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="skip_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">skip breathing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Hypercapnia#Skip_breathing" title="Hypercapnia">Hypercapnia#Skip breathing</a></span></p>
Breathing pattern where the diver holds each breath a while to conserve breathing gas, which can cause <a href="/wiki/Hypercapnia" title="Hypercapnia">hypercapnia</a> which can lead to headaches, aggravate nitrogen narcosis, increase risk of oxygen toxicity, and reduce physiological reserves in an emergency.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="s-lay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">S-lay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Submarine_pipeline#The_S-lay_system" title="Submarine pipeline">Submarine pipeline#The S-lay system</a></span></p>
Method of laying undersea pipelines by welding the sections together on the lay barge and deploying them from the stern horizontally guided by a "stinger" - a structure that supports the pipe string to control its bend radius.<sup id="cite_ref-huismanequipment1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huismanequipment1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The term refers to the shape of the bend in the pipe which transitions from roughly horizontal onboard where the sections are welded together, to angled downward  over the stinger, to roughly horizontal again as it settles on the seabed.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="slate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">slate</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Rigid plastic tablet used for writing messages or notes.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sling_cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sling cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Open-circuit" title="Diving cylinder">Diving cylinder#Open-circuit</a></span></p>
Independent cylinders with their own regulators carried clipped to the harness at the side of the diver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="slingshot_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">slingshot valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § Y-valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#Y-valve" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">Y-valve</a></span></span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Other_distinguishing_features" title="Scuba cylinder valve">Scuba cylinder valve#Other distinguishing features</a></span></p>
A cylinder valve with two valved outlets angled to left and right of the centreline</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="slob_knob" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">slob knob</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Flexible extension used for operating valve knobs on a manifold</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="smb" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SMB</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#surface_marker_buoy"><span title="See entry on this page at § surface marker buoy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">surface marker buoy</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="snag_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">snag line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Line used for underwater search intended to snag on the target. May be dragged by boats or by divers. May be weighted if dragged over a smooth bottom.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="snap_shackle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">snap shackle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Shackle#Snap_shackle" title="Shackle">Shackle#Snap shackle</a></span></p>
A clip connector mechanism which locks when closed, can be operated without tools, and can usually be released under load.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="snoopy_loop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">snoopy loop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rubber_band#Snoopy_loop" title="Rubber band">Rubber band#Snoopy loop</a></span></p>
A heavy duty elastic band made from a slice of inner tube.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="snoot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">snoot</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Underwater_photography#Snoot" title="Underwater photography">Underwater photography#Snoot</a></span></p>
Accessory for a photographic strobe which limits illumination of the subject to a very small area, leaving the background datk, and virtually eliminating backscatter.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="snorkel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">snorkel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Snorkel_(swimming)" title="Snorkel (swimming)">Snorkel (swimming)</a></span></p>
Tube with a bend and mouthpiece used for breathing air from above the water surface when the wearer's mouth and nose are submerged.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="snorkeling" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">snorkeling</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="snorkelling" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">snorkelling</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">Snorkeling</a></span></p>
Swimming at the surface of the water while breathing through a snorkel. the snorkeller is almost always equipped with a diving mask or swim goggles, and usually swimfins.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="snorkel_keeper" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">snorkel keeper</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Snorkel_(swimming)#Construction" title="Snorkel (swimming)">Snorkel (swimming)#Construction</a></span></p> 
Device to hold a snorkel in place at the side of a diving mask by fixing it to the mask strap.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="snuba" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Snuba</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § airline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#airline" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">Hookah</a></span></span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Snuba" title="Snuba">Snuba</a></span></p>
Snuba is a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of "snorkel" and "scuba", referring to a proprietary recreational surface supplied underwater breathing system supplied from a cylinder mounted on a small raft towed by the diver.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="So">So</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: So">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="solo_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">solo diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Solo_diving" title="Solo diving">Solo diving</a></span></p>
The practice of scuba diving alone, without a <a href="/wiki/Buddy_diving" title="Buddy diving">dive buddy</a> or in-water <a href="/wiki/Standby_diver" class="mw-redirect" title="Standby diver">standby diver</a> .</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sonic_orifice" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sonic orifice</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Choked_flow" title="Choked flow">Choked flow</a></span></p>
Metering device to provide constant mass flow of a gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sorb" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sorb</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "sodasorb", "sodalime" and "sofnolime"</span></p>
Carbon dioxide absorbent material used in rebreather or life support system scrubber to remove carbon dioxide from the breathing gas so it may be recycled.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sp">Sp</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sp">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="speargun" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">speargun</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Speargun" title="Speargun">Speargun</a></span></p>
Hunting weapon for shooting fish underwater which propels a barbed steel spear a short distance forward using stored energy from stretched rubber strips or compressed air behind a captive piston.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spearo" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spearo</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Slang term for breathhold spearfisher.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="speech_unscrambler" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">speech unscrambler</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "helium unscrambler" and "unscrambler"</span></p>
An electronic device to render words spoken in a hyperbaric helium environment intelligible.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="speleogen" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">speleogen</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Speleogen" title="Speleogen">Speleogen</a></span></p>
Dissolution features in bedrock.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="speleothem" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">speleothem</dfn></dt>
