<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Speleothem" title="Speleothem">Speleothem</a></span></p>
Also known as a cave formation: A secondary mineral deposit formed in a cave.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spg" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SPG</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#submersible_pressure_gauge"><span title="See entry on this page at § submersible pressure gauge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">submersible pressure gauge</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="sphl" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SPHL</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#self-propelled_hyperbaric_lifeboat"><span title="See entry on this page at § Self-propelled hyperbaric lifeboat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Self-propelled hyperbaric lifeboat</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="spider" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spider</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Full-face_diving_mask#Straps" title="Full-face diving mask">Full-face diving mask#Straps</a></span></p>
Mask strap system for full-face masks with three or more straps. (commonly 5)</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spitcock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spitcock</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Standard_diving_dress#Helmet" title="Standard diving dress">Standard diving dress#Helmet</a></span></p>
A valve in the side of a copper diving helmet which could be used by the diver to suck in a mouthful of seawater to spit onto the inside face of a viewport to wash off condensation droplets to improve their view.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SPM</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#single_point_mooring"><span title="See entry on this page at § single point mooring" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">single point mooring</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="spool" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spool</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href="/wiki/Distance_line#Reels_and_spools" title="Distance line">Distance line#Reels and spools</a></i><br />
Circular device for storing line, comprising a short tubular section with a relatively large flange at each end. No moving parts. A small, compact, economical and reliable alternative to a reel for relatively short lines.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Short, straight section of pipe or tube with a flange at each end.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spread" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spread</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The topside base for (usually) surface supplied commercial diving operations. Also "<span title="See entry on this page at § air spread" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#air_spread" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">air spread</a></span>" and "<a href="#saturation_spread"><span title="See entry on this page at § saturation spread" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">saturation spread</span></a>" (q.v.) depending on the diving mode.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spring" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spring</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrology)" title="Spring (hydrology)">Spring (hydrology)</a></span></p>
Place where a concentrated flow of water emerges from the ground.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spring_strap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spring strap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See:<a href="/wiki/Swimfin#Attachment" title="Swimfin">Swimfin#Attachment</a></span></p>
Fin strap using a stainless steel spring to secure the fin to the foot.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spring_suit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spring suit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Wetsuit" title="Wetsuit">wetsuit</a> that covers the torso and has short sleeves and long or short legs</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spud_can" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">spud can</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The foot on a leg of a <span title="See entry on this page at § Jack-up rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#Jack-up_rig" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">Jack-up rig</a></span> oil platform designed to spread the load so that the rig does not sink too deeply into the sea-bed.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="spums" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SPUMS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Underwater_Medicine_Society" title="South Pacific Underwater Medicine Society">South Pacific Underwater Medicine Society</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="square_profile" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">square profile</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dive_profile#Square_profile" title="Dive profile">Dive profile#Square profile</a></span></p>
Dive profile where the diver descends continuously to the maximum depth and stays there for the duration of the dive before ascending directly at a stedy rate to the surface or first decompression stop. This profile provides worst case exposure for gas absorption by the body tissues for a given depth and bottom time, and is assumed for most decompression planning using decompression tables.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="squeeze" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">squeeze</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § barotrauma" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#barotrauma" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">barotrauma</a></span></span></p>
Injury or discomfort caused by increase or decrease in volume of gas space in the diver's body or equipment due to a change in ambient pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ssde" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SSDE</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving" title="Surface-supplied diving">Surface-supply diving equipment</a>.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="St">St</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: St">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="stabilisor_jacket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stabilisor jacket</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="stab_jacket" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">stab jacket</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#buoyancy_compensator"><span title="See entry on this page at § buoyancy compensator" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buoyancy compensator</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="stage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stage</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <span title="See entry on this page at § diving stage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_stage" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diving stage</a></span></i></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href="#stage_cylinder"><span title="See entry on this page at § stage cylinder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">stage cylinder</span></a></i></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Part of a dive in which gas is breathed from a specific stage cylinder</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="stage_cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stage cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A cylinder used for a stage of a long penetration dive, also known as drop cylinder, which is placed on the distance line to be collected on the return.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Also generically used to refer to decompression gas cylinders carried as <a href="#sling_cylinder"><span title="See entry on this page at § sling cylinder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">sling cylinders</span></a> (q.v.)</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="staged_decompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">staged decompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The practice of making decompression stops.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="stage-drop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stage-drop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Placing a <a href="#stage_cylinder"><span title="See entry on this page at § stage cylinder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">stage cylinder</span></a> at the <span title="See entry on this page at § distance line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#distance_line" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">distance line</a></span> for planned later use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="stage-only_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stage-only diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Terminology" title="Sidemount diving">Sidemount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
The use of standard deco/stage cylinder configuration, without back-mounted cylinders, on an otherwise standard, or partially modified tec/rec BCD. The cylinders are attached to waist and shoulder D-Rings by direct bolt-snap, and no bungee cord is used in the upper attachment. Similar to, and may be confused with <a href="#sidemount"><span title="See entry on this page at § sidemount" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">sidemount</span></a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="standard_diving_dress" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">standard diving dress</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="standard_dress" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">standard dress</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "heavy gear"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Standard_diving_dress" title="Standard diving dress">Standard diving dress</a></span></p>
Early free flow surface supplied diving equipment using a heavy rubberised canvas suit, copper helmet and <span title="See entry on this page at § corselet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#corselet" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">corselet</a></span>, and weighted boots. Still in use in some parts of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="standard_operating_procedure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">standard operating procedure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Standard_operating_procedure" title="Standard operating procedure">Standard operating procedure</a></span></p> 
Procedure compiled by an organisation prescribing the processes to be followed when performing specified tasks.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="standby_diver" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">standby diver</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="stand-by_diver" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">stand-by diver</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Standby_diver" class="mw-redirect" title="Standby diver">Standby diver</a></span></p> 
(Professional) diver functioning as a safety backup to the working diver. Often on the surface at the dive control point, but ready to enter the water at very short notice on the instruction of the supervisor. In bell diving the stand-by diver would be the <a href="/wiki/Bellman_(diving)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bellman (diving)">bellman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="static_apnea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">static apnea</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="static_apnoea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">static apnoea</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Static_apnea" title="Static apnea">Static apnea</a></span></p>
Underwater breath-holding without changing location</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="static_lung_load" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">static lung load</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "hydrostatic imbalance", "SLL"</span></p>
The pressure difference between gas inside the lungs and the gas inside the mouthpiece of the breathing apparatus or inside the helmet. In most rebreathers this is the hydrostatic pressure at depth of the counterlung. In ballasted bellows counterlungs the pressure is modified by the force exerted by the ballast weight.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="steamer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">steamer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A full one piece <a href="/wiki/Wetsuit" title="Wetsuit">Wetsuit</a> that covers the torso and the full length of the arms and legs.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="stinger" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stinger</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An overboard extension at the stern of an offshore pipe lay barge used to provide additional support at the over bend of an S-lay during offshore construction.<sup id="cite_ref-huismanequipment1_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huismanequipment1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="stop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § decompression stop" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#decompression_stop" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">decompression stop</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="living_depth" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">living depth</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#storage_depth"><span title="See entry on this page at § storage depth" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">storage depth</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="storage_depth" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">storage depth</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "living depth"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Saturation_diving#Accommodation" title="Saturation diving">Saturation diving#Accommodation</a></span></p>
Depth pressure in a saturation system at which divers live between compression and decompression when not locked out on a dive.<sup id="cite_ref-NORSOK_U100_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NORSOK_U100-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="stride_entry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stride entry</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "giant stride entry"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries" title="Scuba skills">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
Entry technique from a platform a small to moderate distance above the water surface, which is suitable to stand on before entry. The diver faces the water and steps out with the leading foot, pushing away from the platform with the back foot, and drops into the water while maintaining a vertical posture until fully submerged. It is usually advisable to hold loose equipment against the body, particularly the mask and DV, and if there is no crotch strap, the buoyancy compensator is held to prevent it riding up the torso on impact. The feet can be brought together after initial impact to limit depth of immersion in moderately shallow water, by applying fin thrust downwards.<sup id="cite_ref-BSAC_Sport_Diving_1985_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSAC_Sport_Diving_1985-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="stroke" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">stroke</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Derogatory term used by <a href="/wiki/Doing_It_Right_(scuba_diving)" title="Doing It Right (scuba diving)">DIR</a> zealots to describe divers who do not follow DIR procedures and use DIR approved equipment and configurations.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Su">Su</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Su">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="subcutaneous_emphysema" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">subcutaneous emphysema</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Subcutaneous_emphysema" title="Subcutaneous emphysema">Subcutaneous emphysema</a></span></p>
Gas under the skin resulting from lung overpressure injury.<sup id="cite_ref-USNDM_R6_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNDM_R6-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="submersible_compression_chamber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">submersible compression chamber</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="submersible_decompression_chamber" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">submersible decompression chamber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § closed bell" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#closed_bell" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">closed bell</a></span></span></p>
A closed diving bell, used for transferring divers under pressure to and from the worksite. Particularly if used fpr decompressio.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="submersible_pressure_gauge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">submersible pressure gauge</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "SPG"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Submersible_pressure_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Submersible pressure gauge">Submersible pressure gauge</a></span></p>
Gauge attached to the first stage regulator and used to monitor pressure remaining in the <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder" title="Diving cylinder">diving cylinder</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="suicide_clip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">suicide clip</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Derogatory term for clip mechanisms which are capable of clipping onto a line or other object without the active and intentional intervention of a user.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="suit_blowup" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">suit blowup</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_skills#Dry_suit_blowup" title="Scuba skills">Scuba skills#Dry suit blowup</a></span></p>
Excessive inflation of a dry suit leading to uncontrolled ascent.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sump" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sump</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sump_(cave)" title="Sump (cave)">Sump (cave)</a></span></p>
A passage in a cave that is submerged under water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sump_pack" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sump pack</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Tough waterproof bag with watertight seal used to carry dry equipment in caves, including through water filled passages.<sup id="cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="superoxide_scrubber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">superoxide scrubber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Rebreather scrubber which not only removes carbon dioxide from the exhaled air, but also replenishes the oxygen by chemical reaction.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="supersaturation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">supersaturation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A temporary and thermodynamically unstable condition of a solvent containing more dissolved gas than it can hold in solution over the long term for the prevailing conditions.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="supersaturation_limit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">supersaturation limit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The theoretical pressure ratio between tissue gas concentration and ambient pressure above which the probability of bubble formation is unacceptably high.<sup id="cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="supervised_diver" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Supervised Diver</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Supervised_Diver" class="mw-redirect" title="Supervised Diver">Supervised Diver</a></span></p>
EN 14153-1 / ISO 24801-1 standard competence for recreational scuba diver. The level 1 "Supervised Diver" has sufficient knowledge, skill and experience to dive, in open water, to a recommended maximum depth of 12&#160;m, which do not require in-water decompression stops, under the direct supervision of a dive leader, in groups of up to four level 1 scuba divers per dive leader provided the dive leader is capable of establishing physical contact with all level 1 scuba divers at any point during the dive, only when appropriate support is available at the surface, and under conditions that are equal or better than the conditions where they were trained.<sup id="cite_ref-EUF_1_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUF_1-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="supervisor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">supervisor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § diving supervisor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_supervisor" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diving supervisor</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="supply_lock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">supply lock</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Small lock on a saturation life support habitat for transfer of relatively small items.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="support_diver" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">support diver</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Support_diver" class="mw-redirect" title="Support diver">Support diver</a></span></p>
A voluntary member of a <span title="See entry on this page at § technical diving" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#technical_diving" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">technical diving</a></span> team who acts as a <a href="#stand-by_diver"><span title="See entry on this page at § stand-by diver" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">stand-by diver</span></a> to the primary dive team, or provides in-water logistical support for a dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surd" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SurD</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#surface_decompression"><span title="See entry on this page at § surface decompression" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">surface decompression</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="surf" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surf</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Breaking_wave" title="Breaking wave">Breaking wave</a></span></p>
The mass or line of broken water formed by waves breaking on a shore or reef</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surface_air_consumption_rate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surface air consumption rate</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A measure of air consumption in units of pressure over time, usually psi/minute, adjusted to surface pressure, used to estimate air endurance of a cylinder of specific size. Useful for those who work in imperial units.<sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_4th_ed_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_4th_ed-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> SAC has a constant value for a given diver and represents gas used on the surface at rest.<sup id="cite_ref-SDI_Solo_IG_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDI_Solo_IG-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Surface gas consumption (SGC) is an alternative term referring to alternative breathing gas mixtures. Occasionally also termed surface consumption rate (SCR)<sup id="cite_ref-divetalking_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divetalking-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Scuba_diving_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scuba_diving-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surface_compression_chamber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surface compression chamber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A hyperbaric chamber for surface use for routine decompression or therapeutic recompression.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surface_decompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surface decompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Surface_decompression" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Surface decompression</a></span></p>
A procedure in which some or all of the staged decompression obligation is done in a decompression chamber immediately after surfacing instead of in the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surface_detection_aids" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surface detection aids</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Equipment, such as flags, <a href="/wiki/Surface_marker_buoy" title="Surface marker buoy">surface marker buoys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flare" title="Flare">flares</a>, <a href="/wiki/EPIRB" class="mw-redirect" title="EPIRB">EPIRBs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_beacon" title="Radio beacon">radio beacons</a> mirrors, and <a href="/wiki/Whistle" title="Whistle">whistles</a>,  carried by divers to maintain contact with dive boats or attract rescue when lost at sea.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surface_equivalent_volume" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surface equivalent volume</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § free gas volume" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#free_gas_volume" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">free gas volume</a></span></span></p> 
Gas volume calculated as expanded to surface pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surface_interval" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surface interval</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Surface_interval" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Surface interval</a></span></p>
The time spent by a diver at surface pressure after a dive during which inert gas which was still present at the end of the dive is further eliminated from the tissues.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surface_marker_buoy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surface marker buoy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "SMB"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Surface_marker_buoy" title="Surface marker buoy">Surface marker buoy</a></span></p>
A buoy towed by a diver to indicate the diver's position to people at the surface.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surface_orientated_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surface orientated diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any diving operation in which the diver is decompressed to surface pressure after the dive. Compare to <a href="#saturation_diving"><span title="See entry on this page at § saturation diving" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">saturation diving</span></a> .<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surg" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">SURG</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Southern Underwater Research Group. An organisation based in Cape Town, which publishes marine ecology field guides, dive travel guides and underwater maps.<sup id="cite_ref-SURG_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SURG-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="surge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">surge</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Waves_and_shallow_water" title="Waves and shallow water">Waves and shallow water</a></span></p>
Reciprocating water movement parallel to the bottom surface caused by the passing of a wave overhead, by analogy with the transient linear motion of a ship in the direction of travel also called surge.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="sustained_load_cracking" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">sustained load cracking</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sustained_load_cracking" title="Sustained load cracking">Sustained load cracking</a></span></p>
The development of cracks in a material subjected over long term to static stress significantly less than the yield stress. There is a low but significant risk of this mode of failure in pressure vessels of AA6351 aluminium alloy.<sup id="cite_ref-Luxfer_support_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luxfer_support-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="swell" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">swell</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Swell_(ocean)" title="Swell (ocean)">Swell (ocean)</a></span></p>
A series of surface gravity waves that is not generated by the local wind.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="swim_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">swim line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Line used to space divers across the search area for a swim line search. Each diver holds the line at a distance from the previous diver of somewhat less than twice the visibility distance. The line is used to keep the divers spaced evenly across the search area while swimming perpendicular to the line.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="swimthrough" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">swimthrough</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="swim-through" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">swim-through</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A submerged arch or short tunnel that a diver can swim through without needing to remove equipment. It is usually possible to see natural light at the far end in good visibility and illumination. Usually refers to a natural formation. Technically an overhead environment, but usually with no risk of getting lost, though entrapment may be possible.</dd>


<dt class="glossary" id="tank_factor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tank factor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § baseline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#baseline" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">baseline</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="taravana" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">taravana</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Taravana" title="Taravana">Taravana</a></span></p>
A form of decompression sickness originally observed among Polynesian island natives who habitually did multiple repetitive deep breath-hold dives.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="task_loading" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">task loading</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Task_loading" title="Task loading">Task loading</a></span></p>
A multiplicity of responsibilities leading to an increased risk of failure on the part of the diver to undertake some key basic function which would normally be routine for safety</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="taut_wire_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">taut wire system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A constant tension wire from a vessel to a weight on the seabed used as a reference to detect movement of a dynamically positioned vessel from the reference point.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Te">Te</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Te">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="technical_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">technical diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Technical_diving" title="Technical diving">Technical diving</a></span></p>
An extension of the scope of <a href="/wiki/Recreational_diving" title="Recreational diving">recreational scuba diving</a> to applications with greater technical complexity and higher inherent risk. Definitions vary, but diving with multiple breathing gases, helium based gases, closed circuit rebreathers, or under extensive overheads are generally considered as technical diving. There is no sharp distinction from other forms of recreational diving.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tech_ring" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tech ring</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/D-ring" title="D-ring">D-ring</a> welded to a <span title="See entry on this page at § belt slide" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#belt_slide" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">belt slide</a></span> so that it can not fold down against the webbing. Intended to make it easier to fit and remove snaps.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="temperature_stick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">temperature stick</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="tempstick" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">tempstick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "thermal profile monitor", "TPM"</span></p>
An array of temperature sensors mounted in a rebreather scrubber canister along the path of gas flow to monitor the temperature as an indication of the advance of the exothermic reaction front of the scrubber, providing an indication of scrubber depletion.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tension_leg_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tension leg rig</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tension-leg_platform" title="Tension-leg platform">Tension-leg platform</a></span></p>
A vertically moored floating structure normally used for the offshore production of oil or gas, particularly suited for water depths between 300 and 1500 meters. The platform is permanently moored by means of tethers at each of the structure's corners and virtually all vertical motion of the platform is eliminated.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="test_of_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">test of pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Diagnostic procedure for <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a>. The diver is recompressed, and if the symptoms reduce, it may be assumed that the diver has decompression sickness and hyperbaric treatment will be effective. The test is not entirely reliable<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="test_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">test pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Pressure at which a gas storage cylinder will be hydrostatically tested for revalidation. Usually 1.5 or 1.67 x working pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tethered_ascent" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tethered ascent</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_skills#Emergency_ascents" title="Scuba skills">Scuba skills#Emergency ascents</a></span></p>
Ascent controlled by a line from the diver to a fixed point at the bottom. This may be used to control depth and rate of ascent when the diver has inadvertently lost complete control of buoyancy due to loss of ballast weight, so cannot attain neutral buoyancy at some point during the ascent, and needs to do decompression. CMAS require this skill for their Self-Rescue Diver certification.<sup id="cite_ref-CMAS_SRDTP_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMAS_SRDTP-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tethered_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tethered diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Diving with a lifeline between the diver and a surface tender.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="thalmann_algorithm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Thalmann algorithm</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="#vVAL18"><span title="See entry on this page at § VVAL18" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">VVAL18</span></a></span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Thalmann_algorithm" title="Thalmann algorithm">Thalmann algorithm</a></span></p>
The Exponential/linear decompression algorithm used in the 2008 US Navy decompression tables</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="therapeutic_recompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">therapeutic recompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Hyperbaric_medicine" title="Hyperbaric medicine">Hyperbaric medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Therapeutic_decompression" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Therapeutic decompression</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness#Treatment" title="Decompression sickness">Decompression sickness#Treatment</a></span></p>
A procedure for treating decompression sickness by recompressing the diver, thus reducing bubble size, and allowing the gas bubbles to re-dissolve, then decompressing slowly enough to avoid further formation or growth of bubbles, or eliminating the inert gases by breathing oxygen under pressure</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="therapeutic_schedule" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">therapeutic schedule</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Procedure for hyperbaric treatment involving recompression to relieve symptoms, followed by decompression at a rate unlikely to cause a relapse. Use of special breathing gas, particularly oxygen, to increase the rate of elimination of inert gases is common.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="thermal_profile_monitor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">thermal profile monitor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#temperature_stick"><span title="See entry on this page at § temperature stick" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">temperature stick</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="thermocline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">thermocline</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Thermocline" title="Thermocline">Thermocline</a></span></p>
A thin but distinct layer in a large body of fluid, in which temperature changes more rapidly with depth than it does in the layers above or below</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="thermodynamic_decompression_model" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">thermodynamic decompression model</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#The_no-supersaturation_approach" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#The no-supersaturation approach</a></span></p>
Hypothesis that bubble formation during decompression will not occur provided absolute ambient pressure exceeds the total of the partial gas tensions in the tissue for each gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="thirds" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">thirds</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § rule of thirds" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#rule_of_thirds" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">rule of thirds</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="three_part_shackle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">three part shackle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "bolt and nut shackle", "bolt shackle"</span></p>
A <a href="/wiki/Shackle" title="Shackle">shackle</a> which uses a bolt as the pin, secured with a nut. The nut may be locked with a <a href="/wiki/Split_pin" title="Split pin">split pin</a> for greater security. The bolt may rotate in the shackle under load without great risk of unscrewing the pin</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="through-water_communications" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">through-water communications</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Wireless voice communications transmitted through the water</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="thumb_the_dive" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">thumb the dive</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Terminate the dive by signalling exit to surface at a time or place other than the planned turning point.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="thunderflash" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">thunderflash</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Friction initiated noisy but relatively harmless pyrotechnic device designed for military exercises, with civilian use for diver recall.<sup id="cite_ref-thunderflashes1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thunderflashes1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thunderflashes2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thunderflashes2-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ti">Ti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="time_to_fly" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">time to fly</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The surface interval necessary after diving to reduce tissue gas concentrations to a level where the risk of <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a> due to the pressure reduction experienced in normal commercial airliners is acceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-USNDM_R6_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNDM_R6-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tinnitus" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tinnitus</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Tinnitus" title="Tinnitus">Tinnitus</a></span></p>
The perception of sound within the ear in the absence of corresponding external sound. Usually a constant tone.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tissue_compartments" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tissue compartments</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Tissue_compartments" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Tissue compartments</a></span></p>
Hypothetical body tissues which are designated as fast and slow to describe the rate of saturation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tissue_half_times" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tissue half times</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Tissue_half_times" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Tissue half times</a></span></p>
The time it takes for the tissue to take up or release 50% of the difference in dissolved gas capacity at a changed partial pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tnt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">TNT</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Total Nitrogen Time: Equivalent time of hyperbaric exposure for a repetitive dive used with some decompression tables.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Trinitrotoluene" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinitrotoluene">Trinitrotoluene</a>, a high explosive</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="To">To</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: To">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="toolbox_talk" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">toolbox talk</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "TBT"</span></p>
A meeting held at the start of each shift or prior to any project critical operation, where the diving supervisor or the <a href="/wiki/Diving_supervisor" title="Diving supervisor">diving supervisor</a>’s delegate and shift personnel discuss the forthcoming tasks or jobs and the potential risks and necessary precautions to be taken.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="top_up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">top up</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § air top" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#air_top" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">air top</a></span></span></p>
To reconnect a partially filled cylinder and add gas until the pressure is within tolerance of the required charging pressure when corrected for temperature.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="touch_contact_signals" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">touch contact signals</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § Rimbach system" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#Rimbach_system" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">Rimbach system</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="toynbee_manoeuvre" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Toynbee manoeuvre</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Ear_clearing" title="Ear clearing">Ear clearing</a></span></p>
Method of equalising the middle ears by pinching the nose and swallowing.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="trait_anxiety" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">trait anxiety</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Anxiety#Trait" title="Anxiety">Anxiety#Trait</a></span></p>
A tendency to respond with anxiety in the anticipation of threatening situations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="transect" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">transect</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Transect" title="Transect">Transect</a></span></p>
A path along which one counts and records occurrences of the phenomena of study.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="transfill" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">transfill</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "decant"</span></p>
Fill cylinder with gas by transfer from a cylinder with higher pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="transfill_whip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">transfill whip</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">High pressure hose and end fittings used to <span title="See entry on this page at § decant" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#decant" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">decant</a></span> between cylinders. Usually includes purge valve and may include pressure gauge.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="trauma_shears" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">trauma shears</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "bandage scissors" or "paramedic shears"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Trauma_shears" title="Trauma shears">Trauma shears</a></span></p>
Blunt tipped slightly serrated shears with angled blades sometimes used by divers as a safety cutting implement in place of a knife or line cutter.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="travel_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">travel gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Gas mixture used for descent and ascent when the <span title="See entry on this page at § bottom gas" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bottom_gas" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bottom gas</a></span> is not suitable for breathing at shallower depths.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="traverse" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">traverse</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Pass through a cave by entering at one point and exiting at another.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="treatment_table" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">treatment table</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A depth, time and breathing gas profile designed to treat a diver for <a href="/wiki/Decompression_illness" title="Decompression illness">decompression illness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tremie" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tremie</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Tremie" title="Tremie">Tremie</a></span></p>
A pipe, through which concrete is placed below water level. The top of the tremie is above water and open, and the bottom end is kept below the surface of the poured concrete.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="triangular_profile" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">triangular profile</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A triangular dive profile is one in which, after a descent at constant rate, and a short bottom time at maximum depth, the diver maintains a constant, slow ascent to the surface or first decompression stop. A plot of depth against elapsed time takes a triangular shape.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="triglide" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">triglide</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § belt slider" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#belt_slider" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">belt slider</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="trilam" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">trilam</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Material used for dry suit shells made of a layer of waterproof rubber laminated between two layers of woven textile.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="trimix" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">trimix</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)" title="Trimix (breathing gas)">Trimix (breathing gas)</a></span></p>
Mixture of three gases for breathing. Oxygen, nitrogen and helium are the gases used.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The gas fractions will usually be specified.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="trim_weight" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">trim weight</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Diving_weighting_system#Trim" title="Diving weighting system">Diving weighting system#Trim</a></span></p>
Ballast weight placed to improve a diver's <a href="#trim"><span title="See entry on this page at § trim" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">trim</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tripping_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tripping line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A line attached to the top of an open parachute lifting bag and at the other end to an anchor point. Its purpose is to invert and thus empty the bag if it becomes detached from the load.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="try-dive" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">try-dive</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Guided dive using unfamiliar equipment as a marketing technique, in the hope of convincing the diver that the product is worth buying. Some instruction or guidance on the use and characteristics of the product is usual. Similar in concept to test driving a motor vehicle, and similarly, generally offered to qualified operators, except for rebreathers, where one qualifies on a specific type.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tu">Tu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="tube" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">tube</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "Kelly tubes" or "Kellys"</span></p> 
A seamless transportable compressed gas container, with a water capacity exceeding 150 litres (5.3&#160;cu&#160;ft) but not more than 3,000 litres (110&#160;cu&#160;ft);<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Often mounted horizontally in manifolded groups on a trailer or <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_container" title="Intermodal container">intermodal container</a> frame.<sup id="cite_ref-Kelly_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kelly-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="tup" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">TUP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Saturation_diving#Transfer_under_pressure" title="Saturation diving">Transfer Under Pressure</a>: Transfer of personnel between hyperbaric environments, usually between a closed bell and a saturation system, or between a portable recompression chamber and a multi-occupant chamber</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="turbidity" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">turbidity</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Turbidity" title="Turbidity">Turbidity</a></span></p>
The cloudiness or haziness of a fluid caused by individual particles (suspended solids) that may be invisible to the naked eye, similar to smoke in air</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="turn_the_dive" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">turn the dive</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Start the return on a dive which has reached the planned turning point in terms of depth, time, gas supply or distance.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="twilight_zone" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">twilight zone</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Deeper than 60&#160;m in the sea, or the part of a cave or cavern that has dim but discernible ambient light.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="type_1_wet_bell" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">type 1 wet bell</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_bell#Type_1_wet_bell" title="Diving bell">Diving bell#Type 1 wet bell</a></span></p>
Wet diving bell (q.v.) with no direct supply of gas and services to the bell. Diver umbilicals lead directly to the surface control point.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="type_2_wet_bell" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">type 2 wet bell</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_bell#Type_2_wet_bell" title="Diving bell">Diving bell#Type 2 wet bell</a></span></p>
Wet diving bell (q.v.) with umbilical supply of gas and other services to the bell, from which they are distributed to the divers umbilicals from a control panel in the bell.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="U">U</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: U">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>


<dt class="glossary" id="uba" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">UBA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Underwater Breathing Apparatus: Equipment used to supply breathing gas to an underwater diver. Usually refers to the part of the system carried underwater by the diver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="udt_vest" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">UDT vest</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Underwater Demolition Team vest, An inflatable surface life-jacket worn by underwater demolition teams. Similar in style and a precursor to the horse-collar style buoyancy compensator.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="uhms" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">UHMS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Undersea_and_Hyperbaric_Medical_Society" title="Undersea and Hyperbaric Medical Society">Undersea and Hyperbaric Medical Society</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="umbilical" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">umbilical</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="umbilical_cable" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">umbilical cable</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Umbilical_cable#Diver" title="Umbilical cable">Umbilical cable#Diver</a></span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § bell umbilical" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bell_umbilical" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bell umbilical</a></span>, <span title="See entry on this page at § diver umbilical" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diver_umbilical" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diver umbilical</a></span>, <span title="See entry on this page at § excursion umbilical" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#excursion_umbilical" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">excursion umbilical</a></span>, and <span title="See entry on this page at § ROV umbilical" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#ROV_umbilical" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">ROV umbilical</a></span></span></p> 
Life support hose and cable bundle connection to a surface supplied diver or diving bell. Comprises gas supply hoses, pneumofathometer, a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strength_member&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Strength member (page does not exist)">strength member</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diver_communications#Voice_communications" title="Diver communications">communications</a> cable, and may also include gas reclaim hose, hot water hose and hoses for hydraulic or pneumatic power, and electrical and optical cables for ancillary equipment. Underwater television cameras and cabling can also be carried as a component part of the umbilical or can be taped or banded to it on a temporary basis. Also refers to the power, control and instrument cable for a ROV.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="umbilical_changeout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">umbilical changeout</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Emergency procedure to disconnect the umbilical and connect a replacement in situ during the dive. Usually only used when a delay in recovering the diver or bell is likely.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="umbilical_cutter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">umbilical cutter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">mechanism fitted to a closed bell which allows the occupants to sever the bell umbilical from inside the sealed and pressurised bell in the event of an umbilical snag that prevents bell recovery. The device is typically hydraulically operated using a hand pump inside the bell, and can shear the umbilical at or just above the point where it is fastened to the top of the bell.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="undertow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">undertow</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Undertow_(water_waves)" title="Undertow (water waves)">Undertow (water waves)</a></span></p>
A subsurface flow of water returning seaward from shore as result of wave action</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="underwater_blackout_syndrome" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">underwater blackout syndrome</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "hyperventilation-induced blackout"</span></p>
