Loss of consciousness due to hypoxia during a breath-hold submersion preceded by hyperventilation where alternative causes of blackout have been excluded.<sup id="cite_ref-Pearn_et_al_2015_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pearn_et_al_2015-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pollock_2014_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pollock_2014-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="unscrambler" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">unscrambler</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § speech unscrambler" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#speech_unscrambler" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">speech unscrambler</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="upline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">upline</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "Jersey upline"</span></p>
A fairly substantial natural fibre rope which is deployed from the bottom using a small lift bag to provide the equivalent of a shotline. The lower end is tied off to the bottom, usually on a wreck, and the diver ascends on the line to avoid being swept away from the site by currents. After reaching the surface, the last diver cuts the line and it sinks back down, Natural fibre is used so the line rots away over a few years.<sup id="cite_ref-shipwreckexpo_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shipwreckexpo-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="upstream" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">upstream</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Against the flow.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="upstream_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">upstream valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator#Upstream_vs_downstream" title="Diving regulator">Diving regulator#Upstream vs downstream</a></span></p>
Valve, (usually regulator first stage or demand valve), where the valve mechanism moves against the flow when opening, and the pressure difference over the valve tends to close it.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="upwelling" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">upwelling</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Upwelling" title="Upwelling">Upwelling</a></span></p>
An oceanographic phenomenon that involves wind-driven motion of dense, cooler, and usually nutrient-rich water towards the ocean surface, replacing the warmer, usually nutrient-depleted surface water</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="V">V</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: V">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Va">Va</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Va">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="valsalva_maneuver" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Valsalva maneuver</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Valsalva_maneuver" title="Valsalva maneuver">Valsalva maneuver</a></span></p>
Technique for equalising the middle ear by moderately forceful attempted exhalation against a closed mouth and blocked nose</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="valve_cage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">valve cage</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Valve_cage" title="Scuba cylinder valve">Scuba cylinder valve#Valve cage</a></span></p> 
Structure or frame fitted to scuba cylinder to protect the cylinder valve or manifold and regulator first stage from impact damage and <span title="See entry on this page at § roll-off" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#roll-off" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">roll-off</a></span> .</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="valve_drill" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">valve drill</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Safety exercise in which the diver shuts down, tests regulators and re-opens the manifold valves on a twin set in a specific order.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="valve_guard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">valve guard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">protective structure or frame fitted to the top of a bulk storage cylinder to protect the cylinder valve from mechanical damage.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="van" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">van</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Enclosed portable compartment with diving spread support equipment. Often built into an <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_container" title="Intermodal container">intermodal container</a>. 
Exanples: 
<ul><li>DDC van, containing control panels for deck decompression chamber operation,</li>
<li>Machinery van, containing hydraulic power pack, compressor, air banks or similar equipment</li></ul></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="van_der_waals_equation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Van der Waals equation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Van_der_Waals_equation" title="Van der Waals equation">Van der Waals equation</a></span></p>
Thermodynamic equation of state for a real (non-ideal) gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="vasoconstriction" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">vasoconstriction</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vasoconstriction" title="Vasoconstriction">Vasoconstriction</a></span></p>
The narrowing of blood vessels resulting from contraction of the muscular wall of the vessels, particularly the large arteries and small arterioles.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="vasodilation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">vasodilation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vasodilation" title="Vasodilation">Vasodilation</a></span></p>
The widening of blood vessels resulting from relaxation of smooth muscle cells within the vessel walls, particularly in the large veins, large arteries, and smaller arterioles.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ve">Ve</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ve">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="venous_gas_embolism" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">venous gas embolism</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_(diving)#Bubble_formation,_growth_and_elimination" title="Decompression (diving)">Decompression (diving)#Bubble formation, growth and elimination</a></span></p>
Inert gas bubbles formed in the venous circulation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="venting_breath" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">venting breath</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Breathing pattern intended to vent gas from a rebreather loop, usually by exhaling through the nose.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="vertical_entry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">vertical entry</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="vertical_drop_entry" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">vertical drop entry</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries" title="Scuba skills">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
An entry technique for relatively high drops, up to and sometimes exceeding 3&#160;m. The feet are overlapped and the legs kept straight. The body and head are kept vertical and the mask and DV held against the face with one or both hands, elbows tucked in. The intention is to hit the water vertically, with the least likelihood of knocking off or damaging vital equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-BSAC_Diving_Manual_1982_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSAC_Diving_Manual_1982-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 249">&#58;&#8202;249&#8202;</span></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="vertigo" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">vertigo</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vertigo" title="Vertigo">Vertigo</a></span></p>
A type of dizziness, where there is a feeling of motion when one is stationary.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="vge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">VGE</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#venous_gas_embolism"><span title="See entry on this page at § venous gas embolism" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">venous gas embolism</span></a></span></p></dd>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vi">Vi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Vi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="viewport" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">viewport</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Glass or plastic window on a diving helmet or mask.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Window on a hyperbaric chamber or manned submersible .</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="vip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">VIP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Visual Inspection Programme (US). Annual visual internal inspection of a scuba cylinder.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="visibility" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">visibility</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="viz" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">viz</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Underwater_vision#Visibility" title="Underwater vision">Underwater vision#Visibility</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turbidity" title="Turbidity">turbidity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nephelometry" class="mw-redirect" title="Nephelometry">nephelometry</a></span></p>
The distance through the water at which an object can just be seen against the background. Often defined as the distance at which a <a href="/wiki/Secchi_disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Secchi disc">Secchi disc</a> perpendicular to the sight line can first be seen when moving towards it. It can vary depending on direction illumination, and depth.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="visual_gap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">visual gap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><span title="See entry on this page at § gap" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#gap" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">Gap</a></span> between guidelines which is small enough that each line can be seen from the other.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="visual_jump" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">visual jump</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The procedure of crossing a <a href="#visual_gap"><span title="See entry on this page at § visual gap" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">visual gap</span></a> (q.v.) without the use of a jump line.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="visual_inspection" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">visual inspection</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Internal and external inspection of a pressure vessel as part of revalidation procedure<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="visual_plus" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Visual Plus</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Eddy-current_testing" title="Eddy-current testing">Eddy-current testing</a></span></p>
Crack detection test of parallel neck threads of aluminium cylinders</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="viton" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Viton</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Viton" class="mw-redirect" title="Viton">Viton</a></span></p>
Synthetic elastomer suitable for oxygen service O-rings.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="volume_tank" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">volume tank</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A pressure vessel connected to the outlet of a gas supply and used as a gas reservoir.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="voting_algorithm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">voting algorithm</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="voting_logic" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">voting logic</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Redundancy_(engineering)#Voting_logic" title="Redundancy (engineering)">Redundancy (engineering)#Voting logic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rebreather_diving#Managing_cell_failure_in_an_electronic_rebreather_control_system" title="Rebreather diving">Rebreather diving#Managing cell failure in an electronic rebreather control system</a></span></p>
The logical procedure in which rebreather electronics compare output from multiple sensors when sensors produce significantly different values, suggesting that one or more are faulty, and choose which signals should be ignored, assuming <a href="/wiki/Statistical_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical independence">statistical independence</a> of the sensors, which may not be valid.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="vpm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">VPM</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Varying_Permeability_Model" title="Varying Permeability Model">Varying Permeability Model</a></span></p>
(also Variable permeability model). A decompression model and associated algorithms based on bubble dynamics.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="vval18" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">VVAL18</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "E-L algorithm", "Exponential-Linear algorithm", "Thalmann algorithm"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Thalmann_algorithm" title="Thalmann algorithm">Thalmann algorithm</a></span></p>
Exponential-Linear algorithm used for the 2008 US Navy tables, which assumes exponential ingassing and a combination of linear and exponential outgassing rates.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="W">W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wa">Wa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Wa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="wall_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wall diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Underwater_diving#Diving_environment" title="Underwater diving">Underwater diving#Diving environment</a></span></p>
Recreational scuba diving along the face of a near vertical cliff wall, particularly if the bottom is below the range of the diver's equipment and certification. This requires good buoyancy control.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="water_capacity" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">water capacity</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Of a cylinder: The internal volume. The amount of water it would hold at ambient pressure at 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F)<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="water_trap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">water trap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Mechanism to trap liquid water carried by compressed gas.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="We">We</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: We">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="weight_belt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">weight belt</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_weighting_system#Weight_belt" title="Diving weighting system">Diving weighting system#Weight belt</a></span></p> 
Ballasted waist belt worn by divers to compensate for excess buoyancy. For scuba and freediving, usually easily removed to establish positive buoyancy in an emergency.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="weight_harness" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">weight harness</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_weighting_system#Weight_harness" title="Diving weighting system">Diving weighting system#Weight harness</a></span></p>
Webbing strap system to support diving weights, usually suspended from the shoulders and fastened around the waist. The harness may carry the weights directly, or they may be carried in pockets on the harness. For scuba diving the weights may be arranged for easy shedding.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="weighting_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">weighting system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_weighting_system" title="Diving weighting system">Diving weighting system</a></span></p>
Weights, generally made of lead, to counteract the buoyancy of other diving equipment, and the belts, pockets or harnesses used to support them.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="weight_slider" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">weight slider</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="weight_stop" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">weight stop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § belt slider" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#belt_slider" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">belt slider</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="welding_shield" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">welding shield</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Cover for the viewport area of a helmet or mask to filter excessive light and UV when welding or oxy-arc cutting.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wellhead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wellhead</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wellhead" title="Wellhead">Wellhead</a></span></p>
The assembly at the surface of an oil or gas well that provides the structural and pressure-containing interface for the drilling and production equipment.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wet_bell" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wet bell</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_bell#Structure_of_a_typical_wet_bell" title="Diving bell">Diving bell#Structure of a typical wet bell</a></span></p>
A mobile platform used to deploy and recover divers to and from working depth fitted with an air dome and on board emergency gas supply for use as safe haven in emergencies. There may be a main supply umbilical from the surface providing breathing gas to a manifold inside the wet bell and diver excursion umbilicals terminated at the wet bell, or the divers' umbilicals may be direct from the surface.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wet_filling" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wet filling</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Temperature_change_during_filling" title="Diving cylinder">Diving cylinder#Temperature change during filling</a></span></p> 
Filling scuba cylinders using a water bath for cooling the cylinders.<sup id="cite_ref-Dry_filling_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dry_filling-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wet_notes" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wet notes</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small notebook of waterproof paper carried by some divers<sup id="cite_ref-Jablonski_2006_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jablonski_2006-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wet_pot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wet pot</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Water filled hyperbaric chamber, generally for experimental work or training.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wetsuit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wetsuit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wetsuit" title="Wetsuit">Wetsuit</a></span></p>
A close fitting, thermally-insulating, foam <a href="/wiki/Neoprene" title="Neoprene">neoprene</a> diving suit that allows a limited volume and movement of water inside the suit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="whip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">whip</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Flexible high pressure gas hose with connector at the free end, used for temporary connections. The other end may be permanently connected to an installation or other equipment, or may also have a temporary connector. Whips are commonly named for their intended use, e.g. filling whip, for filling cylinders, decanting, transfill or transfer whip for decanting between cylinders, oxygen whip for oxygen transfer, blending whip, for decanting gases when blending gas, etc. Accessories may include a flow control valve, bleed valve, pressure gauge, and/or whip check.<sup id="cite_ref-Oxyhacker_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxyhacker-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="whip_check" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">whip check</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A cable or webbing strap connecting a hose end to the attachment point in addition to the hose end fitting, which restrains the movement of the hose if the connection is broken under pressure. Whip checks connecting two hose ends may also be attached to an anchor point to limit motion further if this is practicable.<sup id="cite_ref-EGIS_2013_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EGIS_2013-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="whip_sock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">whip sock</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: <span title="See entry on this page at § containment grip" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#containment_grip" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">containment grip</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-Whipchecks_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whipchecks-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></span></p>Whip check device which contains a short section of the whip within a braided tube which reduces wear and point loading on the hose, and constrains motion of the hose end more than a standard whip check in case of disconnection under pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-Whipsocks_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whipsocks-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="wing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Backplate_and_wing" title="Backplate and wing">Backplate and wing</a></span></p>
Back inflation <a href="/wiki/Buoyancy_compensator_(diving)" title="Buoyancy compensator (diving)">buoyancy compensator</a> cell.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wkpp" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">WKPP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Woodville_Karst_Plain_Project" title="Woodville Karst Plain Project">Woodville Karst Plain Project</a>, a project to survey subterranean aquifers in Florida.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wo">Wo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Wo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dt class="glossary" id="woolly_bear" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">woolly bear</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A wool or synthetic pile thermal under-suit worn under a diving <a href="/wiki/Dry_suit" title="Dry suit">dry suit</a>, particularly with <a href="/wiki/Standard_diving_dress" title="Standard diving dress">standard diving dress</a>, often one-piece.<sup id="cite_ref-Rey_2012_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rey_2012-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="working_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">working pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "charging pressure"</span></p> 
Maximum filling pressure rating for the cylinder at standard temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="work_of_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">work of breathing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "WOB"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Work_of_breathing" title="Work of breathing">Work of breathing</a></span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="/wiki/Breathing_performance_of_regulators" title="Breathing performance of regulators">Breathing performance of regulators</a></span></p>
The effort expended in inhaling and exhaling the breathing gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wreck_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wreck diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wreck_diving" title="Wreck diving">Wreck diving</a></span></p>
Recreational or technical diving on and inside of <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">shipwrecks</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="wrist_slate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">wrist slate</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small plastic writing surface attached to the diver's wrist</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="X">X</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: X">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Y">Y</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Y">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>


<dt class="glossary" id="yoke_adaptor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">yoke adaptor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fitting used to connect a regulator or filling whip with a DIN thread connection to a  <span title="See entry on this page at § CGA 850" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#CGA_850" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">CGA 850</a></span> "international" connection cylinder valve.<sup id="cite_ref-Harlow_1999_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harlow_1999-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="yoke_fitting" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">yoke fitting</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fitting used to connect a regulator or filling whip to a diving cylinder using the <span title="See entry on this page at § CGA 850" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#CGA_850" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">CGA 850</a></span> "international" connection.<sup id="cite_ref-Harlow_1999_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harlow_1999-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="yoke_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">yoke valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A valve used to connect a regulator or filling whip to a diving cylinder using the <span title="See entry on this page at § CGA 850" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#CGA_850" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">CGA 850</a></span> "international" connection, mostly used in the US and countries where US diving tourists are economically important.<sup id="cite_ref-Harlow_1999_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harlow_1999-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="y-valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Y-valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "slingshot valve"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Dual_outlet_valves" title="Scuba cylinder valve">Scuba cylinder valve#Dual outlet valves</a></span></p>
Cylinder valve body with two outlets and two valve mechanisms which can be independently controlled so that two regulator first stages can be fitted. Similar to H-valve but in Y configuration.</dd>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Z">Z</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Z">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>


<dt class="glossary" id="zhl-8" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ZHL-8</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="zhl-16" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ZHL-16</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/B%C3%BChlmann_decompression_algorithm" title="Bühlmann decompression algorithm">Bühlmann decompression algorithms</a>. Also ZHL-16a, b and c</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="zip_tie" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">zip tie</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "cable tie", "tie wrap"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cable_tie" title="Cable tie">Cable tie</a></span></p>
Self-locking plastic strip used to connect objects together.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="z-knife" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Z-knife</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Line cutting tool with a replaceable blade in a slot.</dd>
